[1]A Guide to the Tinellbian Languages
This is a grammar of the languages of Tinellb. All these languages descend from a single common ancestor, High Lulani. Lulani and its descendants were taken into each of the Ptokan worlds by the Guozu.
[2]<a href="highlulani/index.html">High Lulani</a>
<high-lulani>WlN</high-lulani> Created by Queen Loren on Mala Ptokonoi.
&date=20180403--------------------------------------------------1
[1]Introduction
The Tinellbian languages are a range of constructed languages, as befits the constructed universe of Tinellb. In that world, the ancestor language was created by Queen Loren of the Ptokonoi, and then evolved naturally as different groups of people moved through space, time and reality.
&date=20171023
--------------------------------------------------2
[1]History
The internal history of the Guozu and their languages is written as if it were a chronicle of actual events. The external history is the more prosaic record: a description of the genesis and evolution of my ideas.&date=20180403--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Internal History
Within the universe named Tinellb, there is a planet named Ptoko. There arose on this world a race of humanoids, the Ptokan. Over millions of years, their race evolved and became the dominant force on their planet.
There had been many conflicts, small and large, throughout their history. One particularly bloody war had had much of the population brought into it: a World War. The survivors of this war were ruled by a single monarch.
Generations passed. The people rebuilt their shattered world. The newest ruler, Queen Loren, decided to create an international language to promote peace amongst her subjects. She named this language Lulani after herself.
Despite their shared language, as more time went by, fractures again showed between nations. Another world war ensued. A great weapon was created, one that tore apart space-time, flinging its victims far out into the universe.
One such group were the Fezhel. They found themselves on an empty world. The Fezhel tongue evolved independently from Lulani, and was later heavily influenced by Zhaladi dialects.
The people that remained on Ptoko slowly grew back towards peace. Their vernacular evolved into Ptokan, and thence into Tsarin. By the time of Tsarin, Lulani was used only for science and the arts, not for everyday use.
Tsarin was spoken in the realm of Tsarein.
[l]HL: High Lulani
VL: Vulgar Lulani

[/l]
&date=20171017
--------------------------------------------------3
[1]External History
I have been interested in language and linguistics since at least the age of 10. I remember making up words when I was quite young. In fact, the High Lulani word <strong>mica</strong> <high-lulani>Mc</high-lulani> <em>hello</em> dates from that time.
When I decided to write a novel, a constructed language (conlang) was an obvious prospect for inclusion in the background information. I had the beginnings of what was to be the Ptokan language, and the language of the Fezhel. The latter  was once designed as a daughter language of Ptokan, but it had some features, mostly phonological, that seemed to come from an earlier language. Thus was Lulani born. Originally intended to be a phonology sketch, Lulani has expanded greatly into a language in its own right. So much so, in fact, that Ptokan and Fezhel have been forced to change somewhat to adapt.
&date=20180316--------------------------------------------------1
[1]High Lulani
High Lulani is the language created by Loren, queen of the Ptokonoi. It features a semi-closed verb class and extensive compounding. It has a featural script.
&date=20170716
--------------------------------------------------2
[1]Phonology
High Lulani phonology has 18 consonant sounds and 3 vowels. Plosives are the only class that have a voicing distinction; fricatives are prototypically voiceless, and resonants are prototypically voiced. Vowels are defined in terms of openness and frontness; there are no oral, length or tone distinctions. All High Lulani words are formed from alternating consonant-vowel pairs. Any word-internal consonant can be geminated, which can palatalise or change the voicing of the original sound.
This page will show each of the International Phonetic Alphabet characters used in High Lulani pronunciations.

[1]Consonants
Consonants are differentiated by manner and place of articulation, and by word-internal gemination. Plosives also have contrasting voice.

[d wordlist]

[e]<strong>nasi&#x294;u</strong> &mdash; geminate word-internal glottal stop
[e]<strong>&rsquo;usu</strong> &mdash; usual glottal stop within sentence
[e]<strong>&#x294;usu</strong> &mdash; capitalised glottal stop at beginning of sentence
[e]<strong>&#x294;allisi</strong> &mdash; capitalised glottal stop for proper noun (Alice)

[2]Stops
Stops are differentiated by voicing, although voiced consonants tend to be rarer than their voiceless counterparts.
The voiced stops are fully voiced word-internally and partially voiced word-initially. Voiced geminate stops are given breathy voice. Voiceless stops are lightly aspirated, which is suppressed in voiceless geminate stops.
Geminate stops are held for approximately twice as long as non-geminate stops.
[3]Labials
The plosives <ipa>/p/</ipa> and <ipa>/b/</ipa> are bilabial.

[3]Glottal
The glottal stop <ipa>/&#x294;/</ipa> is on<em>e</em> of the most common sounds. Non-geminate glottal stops are often suppressed between unstressed vowels. The second of a geminate glottal stop becomes a palatal approximant <ipa>/j/</ipa>.

[/d]
[2]Nasals
There are nasal consonants at each of the places of articulation of the plosives. However, the palatal nasal is only found when geminating the alveolar nasal. Nasals are prototypically voiced. Geminate nasals are held for 1 &frac12; times as long as non-geminates.
[3]Labial
The labial nasal <ipa>/m/</ipa> is bilabial.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mana.html#highlulani">mana</a> <ipa>/&#x2c8;<strong>m</strong>an.&#x259;/</ipa> <high-lulani>mn</high-lulani> <em>bubble</em>

[3]Alveolar
The alveolar nasal <ipa>/n/</ipa> is apical. When geminated, this sound is palatal and laminal.

[3]Velar
The nasal <ipa>/&#x14b;/</ipa> is velar.

[2]Liquids
The liquids are mainly differentiated by laterality. This language lacks phonemic glides. Like nasals, approximants are prototypically voiced, and geminates are held for 1 &frac12; times as long as non-geminates.
The consonant <ipa>/l/</ipa> is lateral and apical. When geminated, this sound is laminal and palatal.
The consonant <ipa>/&#x27e;/</ipa> is central, retroflex and sub-apical. When geminated, this sound becomes a trill.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lassi.html#highlulani">lassi</a> <ipa>/&#x2c8;<strong>l</strong>as.s&#x268;/</ipa> <high-lulani>l;S</high-lulani> <em>baby</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kulu.html#highlulani">kulu</a> <ipa>/&#x2c8;k&#x2b0;u<strong>l</strong>.&#x289;/</ipa> <high-lulani>&gt;W</high-lulani> <em>fork</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/malliju.html#highlulani">malliju</a> <ipa>/&#x2c8;ma<strong>&#x28e;.&#x28e;</strong>&#x268;.&#x25f;&#x289;/</ipa> <high-lulani>m;LY</high-lulani> <em>happiness</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru'iha.html#highlulani">ru&rsquo;iha</a> <ipa>/<strong>&#x27d;</strong>&#x289;.&#x2c8;&#x294;ih.&#x259;/</ipa> <high-lulani>wih</high-lulani> <em>history</em>

[2]Fricatives
Fricatives do not have complete closure of the vocal tract, but are formed with enough constriction to bring turbulence to the airstream.
Fricatives are prototypically voiceless. The lips remain unrounded for all fricatives unless followed or preceded by a rounded vowel. Geminate fricatives are held for 1 &frac12; times as long as non-geminates.
[3]Labial
The fricative <ipa>/f/</ipa> is realised as labiodental.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/faxi.html#highlulani">faxi</a> <ipa>/&#x2c8;<strong>f</strong>a&#x255;.&#x268;/</ipa> <high-lulani>fX</high-lulani> <em>to survive</em>

[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'iffa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;iffa</a> <ipa>/&#x2c8;&#x294;i<strong>f.f</strong>&#x259;/</ipa> <high-lulani>i;f</high-lulani> <em>it</em>
[3]Alveolar
The fricative <ipa>/s/</ipa> is apical.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sikka.html#highlulani">sikka</a> <ipa>/&#x2c8;<strong>s</strong>ik.k&#x259;/</ipa> <high-lulani>S;k</high-lulani> <em>skin</em>

[3]Palatal
The palatal fricative <ipa>/&#x255;/</ipa> is laminal.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xaha.html#highlulani">xaha</a> <ipa>/&#x2c8;<strong>&#x255;</strong>ah.&#x259;/</ipa> <high-lulani>xh</high-lulani> <em>name</em>

[3]Glottal
The fricative <ipa>/h/</ipa> is a voiceless sound. When geminate, it is pronounced as a palatal fricative.

[1]Vowels
There are three phonemic vowels, with three main allophones for each. The vowels are distinguished by closeness and frontness.
[t]|h front |h central |h back
h close | <ipa>i</ipa> | <ipa>(&#x268;) (&#x289;)</ipa> | <ipa>u</ipa>
h mid || <ipa>(&#x259;)</ipa>
h open | <ipa>a</ipa>
[/t]
[d mobile-table]
<strong>close:</strong>
[e]<strong>front:</strong> <ipa>i</ipa>
[e]<strong>central:</strong> <ipa>(&#x268;) (&#x289;)</ipa>
[e]<strong>back:</strong> <ipa>u</ipa>

There are three phonemic vowels: two close vowels and one open. These are given in the above chart, with the variant allophones in (round brackets). The central and mid vowels are considered the lax variants, while the lengthened vowels are long.
[2]Front
The front close vowel is unrounded. It is realised as <ipa>/i/</ipa> or <ipa>/&#x268;/</ipa>.

[2]Open
The open vowel is unrounded. It can be realised as <ipa>/a/</ipa> or <ipa>/&#x259;/</ipa>.

[2]Back
The back close vowel is rounded. It can be realised as <ipa>/u/</ipa> or <ipa>/&#x289;/</ipa>.

[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tu.html#highlulani">tu</a> <ipa>/t&#x2b0;<strong>u&#x2d0;</strong>/</ipa> <high-lulani>e</high-lulani> <em>child</em>&date=20180323--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Phonotactics
Phonemically, all syllables are CV, that is, one consonant followed by one vowel. Word-internal consonants can be geminated. The only consonant clusters are geminate consonants, and there are no vowel clusters or long vowels.&date=20180323--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Suprasegmentals
[2]Syllabication
Syllable breaks are placed between two geminate consonants.
[d wordlist]
[e]bat.ta
[/d]
If there are no geminates, then the final vowel, and every second vowel going backwards are their own syllables.
[d wordlist]
[e]tuc.i
[e]lu.lan.i
[e]pam.i.lam.i
[/d]
These two rules are in order of priority, and two closed syllables can only appear next to one another if they both end in geminates, thus:
[d wordlist]
[e]jan.ni.ga
[e]rad.dil.la
[/d]
[2]Stress
Primary stress falls on the last closed syllable, and secondary stress on the penultimate closed syllable. Stress is characterised by a slightly longer vowel and an altered pitch: high for primary, low for secondary.
[e]b&aacute;t.ta
[e]t&uacute;c.i
[e]lu.l&aacute;n.i
[e]p&agrave;m.i.l&aacute;m.i
[e]j&aacute;n.ni.ga
[e]rad.d&iacute;l.la
[2]Prosody
Interrogative and imperative sentences (questions and orders) are denoted by tone. This tone is either a rising tone (&#x1ce;) or a falling tone (&acirc;), placed on the syllable of the appropriate word which has the greatest stress.
Falling tone can also be used to bring focus to a particular word.
&date=20180323--------------------------------------------------2
[1]Orthography
As well as the syllabary for most written use, there are also special-use syllabaries. One of these encodes more redundancy for use with noisy channels. The other is a non-visual written code for blind and other visually impaired users.&date=20180323--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Syllabary
The Lulani syllabary was developed as a featural script, with similar sounds having similar symbols.
It is written in horizontal rows, right-to-left, and top-to-bottom.

Geminate consonants are shown as <high-lulani>;</high-lulani>, placed before the geminated consonant.
A central dot <high-lulani>/</high-lulani> is placed between words, and sentences begin and end with a <high-lulani>.</high-lulani> symbol.
While their shapes have been modified over time, it is still fairly clear how each phonetic feature has been symbolised.
[l]stop: (none)
nasal: vertical stroke
fricative: arc
lateral: swish
flap: loop
labial: low circle
alveolar / retroflex: apex
palatal: corner
velar: semi-circle
glottal: high circle
open vowel: (none)
front vowel: vertical line
back vowel: horizontal line
[/l]
&date=20180324--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Spelling Syllabary
There is a spelling syllabary, used for transmitting words across potentially noisy communication channels, such as telephone lines. It is also used for communicaing in situations where every syllable is important, such as giving names. Each syllable corresponds to a disyllabic word, which begins with the same consonant and ends with its vowel. The geminate symbol is represented by the word <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fa''a.html#highlulani">fa&#x294;a</a> <em>language</em>.

[1]Tactile Syllabary
There is a tactile syllabary for use by blind and visually-impaired language users.
Each cell is three rows by two columns of raised dots. The upper four dots generally denote the consonant, with syllables beginning with b, d, j, g, f, or x being the exceptions. The lowest pair generally denote the vowel.

Dot 5 (&#x2810;) by itself is the geminate. Word separation is shown by (&#x2800;) an empty space, clause separation by (&#x2824;) the comma, and sentence separation by (&#x2814;) the period. Numbers are prefixed with (&#x2828;) the number sign, and the first syllable of each number is used.
&date=20180324--------------------------------------------------2
[1]Morphology
High Lulani is an analytic agglutinative language, as morphemes tend to keep their own shape, even when forming words.&date=20180324--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Nouns
Common and proper nouns are open classes; the pronouns are closed.
[2]Common Nouns
Common nouns can refer to abstract or concrete items.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <high-lulani>Wi</high-lulani> <em>love</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/bata.html#highlulani">bata</a> <high-lulani>bt</high-lulani> <em>caution</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'ahati.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ahati</a> <high-lulani>ahT</high-lulani> <em>happiness</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/caga.html#highlulani">caga</a> <high-lulani>cg</high-lulani> <em>mouth</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/purissiji.html#highlulani">purissiji</a> <high-lulani>oR;SJ</high-lulani> <em>circle</em>[/d]
[3]Stem Nouns
Stem nouns are those that are neither compounded nor derived.
[4]Mass Nouns
Mass nouns refer to an undifferentiated aggregation rather than separate units. These cannot take numbers, except for a postpended <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xita.html#highlulani">xita</a> <em>one</em> to denote the smallest individual piece of that aggregate.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'iti.html#highlulani">&rsquo;iti</a> <high-lulani>iT</high-lulani> <em>milk</em> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'iti.html#highlulani">&rsquo;iti</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xita.html#highlulani">xita</a> <high-lulani>iTXt</high-lulani> <em>drop of milk</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/marru.html#highlulani">marru</a> <high-lulani>m;w</high-lulani> <em>flies</em> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/marru.html#highlulani">marru</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xita.html#highlulani">xita</a> <high-lulani>m;wXt</high-lulani> <em>fly</em>[/d]
[4]Animacy
This determines which derivational suffixes can be applied, and which pronouns are used as reference.
[5]Animate Noun
These refer to people and other multicellular organisms capable of independent movement.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gusu.html#highlulani">gusu</a> <high-lulani>&lt;z</high-lulani> <em>person</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a> <high-lulani>WlN</high-lulani> <em>queen</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kitisu.html#highlulani">kitisu</a> <high-lulani>KTz</high-lulani> <em>father</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sula.html#highlulani">sula</a> <high-lulani>zl</high-lulani> <em>goat</em>
[/d]
[5]Inanimate Noun
These refer to things such as natural phenomena, plants, fungi and unicellular life.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tissa.html#highlulani">tissa</a> <high-lulani>T;s</high-lulani> <em>wind</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/linu.html#highlulani">linu</a> <high-lulani>LI</high-lulani> <em>tree</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hurru.html#highlulani">hurru</a> <high-lulani>V;w</high-lulani> <em>yeast</em>[/d]
[5]Abstract Noun
This category encompasses concepts, ideas and other intangibles. They are referred to by inanimate pronouns.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sutti.html#highlulani">sutti</a> <high-lulani>z;T</high-lulani> <em>fear</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'adda.html#highlulani">&rsquo;adda</a> <high-lulani>a;d</high-lulani> <em>past</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tuhhi.html#highlulani">tuhhi</a> <high-lulani>e;H</high-lulani> <em>agriculture</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/laru.html#highlulani">laru</a> <high-lulani>lw</high-lulani> <em>year</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sajja.html#highlulani">sajja</a> <high-lulani>s;j</high-lulani> <em>silence</em>[/d]
[3]Compound Nouns
The first part of a compound noun must be a noun, and the subsequent parts specify the meaning of that noun. These parts can be nouns or verbs. The whole noun is usually written without spaces. The syllabification and stress of nonce words are determined on a stem-by-stem basis. However, a compound in common use will start being treated whole.

[2]Proper Nouns
Proper nouns begin with a capital letter in the transliteration. These are names that refer to individual people, places or things.

[1]Pronouns
Pronouns are a closed class. They are marked for case and person. The third person pronouns are additionally marked for <a href="../deixis.html#topicality">topicality</a> or <a href="index.html#animacy">animacy</a>.

[2]Person
First person refers to the speaker or speakers, and any group for whom they are speaking.
Second person refers to the listener or listeners, and any group the listener is representing.
Third person refers to any other party. It is not used for the subject of the sentence, whether present or implied.
[2]Number
Pronouns are not marked for number. However, if the pronoun refers to a group that includes more than one of these persons, then additional pronouns can be constructed as follows:
The second person transitive pronoun <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">fu</a> <high-lulani>v</high-lulani> can be suffixed to the first person pronouns to form first person inclusive plural pronouns.
The third person intransitive inanimate pronoun <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a> <high-lulani>p</high-lulani> can be suffixed to any first or second person pronouns, including those with <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">fu</a>, to form other plural pronouns.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/suma.html#highlulani">suma</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">fu</a> <high-lulani>zmv</high-lulani> <em>you and I</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pixi.html#highlulani">pixi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">fu</a> <high-lulani>PXv</high-lulani> <em>to you and me</em>

[2]The Genitive
Four of the cases are used to mark a connection between the noun and the main verb of the clause. Contrariwise, the function of the genitive is to mark a connection between nouns, including one noun possessing another.
[3]Alienable Possession
Possession is alienable when the possessed item can be transferred from one owner to another. Alienable possessions include objects bought or received by a person.
The structure of the possessive phrase for alienable possession is &ldquo;<em>possessor</em> <strong>genitive</strong> <em>possessed&rdquo;.</em> The genitive marker marks the animacy of the possessor.

[3]Inalienable Possession
Inalienable possession refers to items which are unable to be transferred from one individual to another. Inalienable possessions include relatives, parts of the body and objects created by a person.
For inalienable possession, as well as genitive constructions that do not involve literal possession, the structure is &ldquo;<em>possessed</em>-<strong>genitive</strong> <em>possessor</em>&ldquo;, that is, the genitive marker is an enclitic on the possessed item. This marker is always the third person inanimate genitive pronoun, unless the possessor is a plain pronoun.

[3]Contrasts
Because of the nature of alienability, some contrasts can be made between possessives.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/luffu.html#highlulani">luffu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pagu.html#highlulani">pagu</a> <em>my eyes, the ones with which I was born</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pagu.html#highlulani">pagu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/luffu.html#highlulani">luffu</a> <em>the eyes I just bought and have in my hand</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'asilari.html#highlulani">&rsquo;asilari</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/ba.html#highlulani">ba</a> <em>your friend</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/ba.html#highlulani">ba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'asilari.html#highlulani">&rsquo;asilari</a> <em>the friend you own</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hu'asa.html#highlulani">hu&rsquo;asa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/disi.html#highlulani">disi</a> <em>the painting she made</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/disi.html#highlulani">disi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hu'asa.html#highlulani">hu&rsquo;asa</a> <em>the painting she bought</em>
Alienable possession is used in a hierarchy when the possessor is of higher rank than the possessed, and inalienable possession when the relationship is the other way around.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pagu.html#highlulani">pagu</a> <em>my queen</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pagu.html#highlulani">pagu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mifasu.html#highlulani">mifasu</a> <em>my vassal</em>
&date=20180327--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Verbs
A verb is a necessary part of any sentence, except when making <a href="../syntax/matrixclauses.html#copularsentences">copular sentences</a>. Verbs can be categorised on the basis of how many elements compose them.
[2]Stem Verbs
The class of stem verbs is semi-closed &mdash; there are only about 100 pure verbs in the entire language. Stem verbs consist of a single element.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'i.html#highlulani">&rsquo;i</a> <high-lulani>i</high-lulani> <em>to say</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dissu.html#highlulani">dissu</a> <high-lulani>D;z</high-lulani> <em>to feel</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a> <high-lulani>us</high-lulani> <em>to see</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a> <high-lulani>j;N</high-lulani> <em>to move</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kissa.html#highlulani">kissa</a> <high-lulani>K;s</high-lulani> <em>to fight</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a> <high-lulani>M&gt;</high-lulani> <em>to be red</em>
[/d]
[2]Compound Verbs
In order to extend or specify meaning,  verbs can be compounded much as a noun can. Compound verbs are, however, much more common than compound nouns, to make up for the relative lack of stem verbs.

[1]Intransitivity
Intransitive verbs are monovalent. For the archetypal intransitives, the verbal patient is the <strong>subject</strong>.

[2]Adjectival Verbs
These verbs allow the speaker to describe an attribute of the <strong>subject</strong>.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Linu ra&rsquo;u ki. / Linu qixa ki.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.LI / Qx / K .  / LI / ru / K.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/linu.html#highlulani">Linu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ki.html#highlulani">ki</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/linu.html#highlulani">Linu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ki.html#highlulani">ki</a>.
[e]<em>Tree</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span> <em>big</em>. / <em>Tree</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;dyn</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present dynamic</span></span> <em>big</em>.
[e]&ldquo;The tree is big. / The tree is growing.&rdquo;
[/d]
The actor who imparts such an attribute is put in the <strong>ablative</strong> case.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Juffila kaluMa&rsquo;iliguna pani.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.Y;Fl / kWmiL&lt;n / pN.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/juffila.html#highlulani">Juffila</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu-.html#highlulani">kalu-</a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maelgwn_Gwynedd">Ma&rsquo;iliguna</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pani.html#highlulani">pani</a>.
[e]<em>Dragon</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>abl</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">ablative</span></span>-Maelgwn <em>tame</em>.
[e]&rdquo;The dragon was tamed by Maelgwn.&rdquo;
[/d]
The experiencer who perceives such an attribute is put in the <strong>dative</strong> case.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Liqu kuhisuba bi&rsquo;u.</strong>

[3]Chromatic Verbs
These are adjectival verbs specifically dealing with <a href="../../apocrypha/colours.html">colour</a>.
[d wordlist]

[2]Kinetic Verbs
These verbs deal with motion of the <strong>subject</strong>. The origin of the movement is in <strong>ablative</strong> case, the destination in <strong>dative</strong>, and the general direction is marked with the adposition <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a>.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a> <high-lulani>j;N</high-lulani> <em>to accelerate; to move around</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'ussa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ussa</a> <high-lulani>u;s</high-lulani> <em>to follow</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nura.html#highlulani">nura</a> <high-lulani>Ir</high-lulani> <em>to leave; to be apart from</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/madi.html#highlulani">madi</a> <high-lulani>mD</high-lulani> <em>to rise; to be high</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ka'u.html#highlulani">ka&rsquo;u</a> <high-lulani>ku</high-lulani> <em>to jump</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hussu.html#highlulani">hussu</a> <high-lulani>V;z</high-lulani> <em>to fall; to be low</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/saja.html#highlulani">saja</a> <high-lulani>sj</high-lulani> <em>to lie down; to be lying down</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tiku.html#highlulani">tiku</a> <high-lulani>T&gt;</high-lulani> <em>to turn</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/na.html#highlulani">na</a> <high-lulani>n</high-lulani> <em>to turn towards; to face</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/raca.html#highlulani">raca</a> <high-lulani>rc</high-lulani> <em>to be hung; to be hanging</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fiqu.html#highlulani">fiqu</a> <high-lulani>FA</high-lulani> <em>to float; to be floating</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tihu.html#highlulani">tihu</a> <high-lulani>TV</high-lulani> <em>to move to; to abide</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/malu.html#highlulani">malu</a> <high-lulani>mW</high-lulani> <em>to move to; to be in a place</em>[/d]
[2]Quasi-Transitive Verbs
These are intransitive verbs in that they do not require a noun phrase in the object position. However, they act transitively by having a second noun phrase marked in a particular way.
[3]Oblique Arguments
These are marked with an <a href="../../syntax/case.html#obliquecases">oblique case marker</a>:
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Luna kalujifiru&rsquo;i mala; luna kalu&rsquo;ilupagu mala.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.Wn / kWJFwi / ml , Wn / kWiWp&lt; / ml.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/luna.html#highlulani">Luna</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu-jifiru'i.html#highlulani">kalu-jifiru&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mala.html#highlulani">mala</a>; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/luna.html#highlulani">luna</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu-'ilu-pagu.html#highlulani">kalu-&rsquo;ilu-pagu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mala.html#highlulani">mala</a>.
[e]<em>Moon</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>abl</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">ablative</span></span>-<em>lake reflect; moon</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>abl</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">ablative</span></span>-<em>heart</em>-<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1gen</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person genitive</span></span> reflect.
[e]&ldquo;The moon is reflected in the lake; the moon is reflected in my heart.&rdquo;
[/d]
The usual case assignment for objects of each of these verbs is shown here:
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mala.html#highlulani">mala</a> <high-lulani>ml</high-lulani> <em>to reflect</em> &mdash; <strong>ablative</strong>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/faxi.html#highlulani">faxi</a> <high-lulani>fX</high-lulani> <em>to survive</em> &mdash; <strong>dative</strong>[/d]
[3]Comparatives
These verbs are used to denote the degree of similarity between two nouns. Their nuance can be modified by use of different case markers or adpositions.
Case denotes unmarked similarity or difference, <strong>dative</strong> for the former, <strong>ablative</strong> for the latter.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Nimalu kuquliruxita runihi.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.NmW / &gt;ALwXt / wNH.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nimalu.html#highlulani">Nimalu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku-.html#highlulani">ku-</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/quliru.html#highlulani">quliru</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xita.html#highlulani">xita</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/runihi.html#highlulani">runihi</a>.
[e]<em>Bear</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>dat</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">dative</span></span>-<em>family-one similar.</em>
[e]&ldquo;The bear is like one of the family.&rdquo;
[/d]
The adposition <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/haru.html#highlulani">haru</a> <high-lulani>hw</high-lulani> <em>with</em> denotes a slight similarity or difference.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>&#x294;usu ra&rsquo;u haruxissatanissa runihi.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.uz / ru / hwX;stN;s / wNH.</high-lulani>
[e][f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&#x294;usu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/haru.html#highlulani">haru</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xissatanissa.html#highlulani">xissatanissa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/runihi.html#highlulani">runihi</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span> <em>with-musician similar.</em>
[e]&ldquo;I am somewhat of a musician.&rdquo;
[/d]
The adpositions <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'adi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;adi</a> <high-lulani>aD</high-lulani> <em>near</em> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xidu.html#highlulani">xidu</a> <high-lulani>XE</high-lulani> <em>far</em> denote a large similarity or difference.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Mari ra&rsquo;u xidupajiga tina.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.mR / ru / XEpJg / Tn.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mari.html#highlulani">Mari</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xidu.html#highlulani">xidu</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pajiga.html#highlulani">pajiga</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tina.html#highlulani">tina</a>.
[e]<em>This</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span> <em>far-olive different</em>.
[e]&ldquo;This is nothing like an olive.&rdquo;
[/d]
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/runihi.html#highlulani">runihi</a> <high-lulani>wNH</high-lulani> <em>to be similar to</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tina.html#highlulani">tina</a> <high-lulani>Tn</high-lulani> <em>to be different from</em>
[/d]
[3]Symmetric Relations
The participants of these verbs are equivalent to each other, that is, if Alice acts on Bob, then Bob acts on Alice in the same way. When the subject is Alice, say, then Bob can:
1. Be placed in the object position. Despite the structure, this is not transitive, as the verb has no <a href="../../syntax/argumentpromotion.html#passive">passive</a>, and pronouns use the intransitive form:
[d folding]
[f]<strong>&#x294;allisi sisa Bubu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.a;LS / Ss / OO.</high-lulani>
[e]&#x294;allisi <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sisa.html#highlulani">sisa</a> Bubu.
[e]<em>Alice contact Bob</em>.
[e]&ldquo;Alice is touching Bob.&rdquo;
[/d]
2. Take <strong>dative</strong> marking:
[d folding]
[f]<strong>&#x294;allisi kuBubu ju&rsquo;i.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.a;LS / &gt;OO / Yi.</high-lulani>
[e]&#x294;allisi <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku-.html#highlulani">ku-</a>Bubu <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ju'i.html#highlulani">ju&rsquo;i</a>.
[e]<em>Alice</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>dat</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">dative</span></span><em>-Bob link</em>.
[e]&ldquo;Alice is married to Bob.&rdquo;
[/d]
3. Be conjoined with the <strong>subject</strong>:
[d folding]
[f]<strong>&#x294;allisi Bubuta hulla</strong>.
[e]<high-lulani>.a;LS / OOt / V;l.</high-lulani>
[e]&#x294;allisi Bubu<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/-ta.html#highlulani">-ta</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hulla.html#highlulani">hulla</a>.
[e]<em>Alice Bob-and copulate.</em>
[e]&ldquo;Alice and Bob are having sex.&rdquo;
[/d]
The basic meaning of these sentences is not changed when swapping the particpants or using the alternate structures.
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sisa.html#highlulani">sisa</a> <high-lulani>Ss</high-lulani> <em>to touch</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ju'i.html#highlulani">ju&rsquo;i</a> <high-lulani>Yi</high-lulani> <em>to join</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hulla.html#highlulani">hulla</a> <high-lulani>V;l</high-lulani> <em>to copulate; to have consumated</em>
[/d]
&date=20180403--------------------------------------------------4
[1]Transitivity
The divalent verbs are called transitive, and these require an object to complete its meaning. It is possible to elide this object if it is obvious or irrelevant. The <strong>subject</strong> is the agent, and the <strong>object</strong> is the patient.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Nimalu dasi (nukki).</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.NmW / dS / I;K.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nimalu.html#highlulani">Nimalu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nukki.html#highlulani">nukki</a>).
[e]<em>Bear eat (strawberry)</em>.
[e]&ldquo;The bear is eating (the strawberry).&rdquo;[/d]
[d wordlist]
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> <high-lulani>dS</high-lulani> <em>to consume</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nidu.html#highlulani">nidu</a> <high-lulani>NE</high-lulani> <em>to use</em>[/d]
[2]Transformative Verbs
Unlike those above, these verbs involve a fundamental change to their <strong>objects</strong>.
[d wordlist]
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'idu.html#highlulani">&rsquo;idu</a> <high-lulani>iE</high-lulani> <em>to make</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pifa.html#highlulani">pifa</a> <high-lulani>Pf</high-lulani> <em>to create</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pura.html#highlulani">pura</a> <high-lulani>or</high-lulani> <em>to change; to be</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/si'a.html#highlulani">si&rsquo;a</a> <high-lulani>Sa</high-lulani> <em>to repair</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lakka.html#highlulani">lakka</a> <high-lulani>l;k</high-lulani> <em>to break</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qarri.html#highlulani">qarri</a> <high-lulani>q;R</high-lulani> <em>to open</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/turu.html#highlulani">turu</a> <high-lulani>ew</high-lulani> <em>to close</em>
[/d]
[2]Motive Verbs
The unmarked argument structure is as follows: the oblique arguments for these are the same as for <a href="intransitivity.html#kineticverbs">kinetic</a> verbs,<em> i.e.:</em> <strong>ablative</strong> <em>source</em>, <strong>dative</strong> <em>destination</em>, and <em>direction</em> with <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a>. As for the core arguments, the agent of the movement is the <strong>subject</strong>, and the patient being moved is the <strong>object</strong>.
[3]Dative
These are motive verbs focussing on movement <em>to</em> the destination.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Suma gi pa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.zm / G / p.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/suma.html#highlulani">suma</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gi.html#highlulani">gi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person transitive</span></span> <em>carry</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ina;int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">inanimate third person intransitive</span></span>.
[e]&ldquo;I picked it up.&rdquo;[/d]
The agent may be moved into the <strong>dative</strong> position, since it is identical to the destination.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Pixi duci &rsquo;iffa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.PX / EC / i;f.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pixi.html#highlulani">Pixi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/duci.html#highlulani">duci</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'iffa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;iffa</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person intransitive</span></span> <em>own</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ina;tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">inanimate third person transitive</span></span>.
[e]<em>lit:</em> &ldquo;(I) own it to me.&rdquo;
[e]&ldquo;It&rsquo;s mine.&rdquo;[/d]
An animate source may be swapped with the patient, <em>i.e.:</em> the <strong>ablative</strong> becoming an <strong>object</strong> and vice versa.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>&#x294;usu ku tali fu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.;uz / &gt; / tL / v.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&#x294;usu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku.html#highlulani">ku</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tali.html#highlulani">tali</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">fu</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ina;dat</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">inanimate third person dative</span></span> <em>take</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person transitive</span></span>.
[e]<em>lit:</em> &ldquo;I took you to it.&rdquo;
[e]&ldquo;I&rsquo;ve relieved you of it.&rdquo;[/d]
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/duci.html#highlulani">duci</a> <high-lulani>EC</high-lulani>  <em>to gain; to possess</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gi.html#highlulani">gi</a> <high-lulani>G</high-lulani> <em>to pick up; to carry</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tali.html#highlulani">tali</a> <high-lulani>tL</high-lulani> <em>to take</em>[/d]
[3]Ablative
These are motive verbs focussing on movement <em>away</em> from a source.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Suma maku pa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.zm / m&gt; / p.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/suma.html#highlulani">Suma</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/maku.html#highlulani">maku</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person transitive</span></span> <em>throw</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ina;int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">inanimate third person intransitive</span></span>.
[e]&ldquo;I threw it.&rdquo;[/d]
Similarly to dative motive verbs, the agent can be placed in <strong>ablative</strong> position, as they are identical to the source.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Puttu funi &rsquo;iffa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.o;e / vN / i;f.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/puttu.html#highlulani">Puttu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/funi.html#highlulani">funi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'iffa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;iffa</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1abl</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person ablative</span></span> <em>lack</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ina;tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">inanimate third person transitive</span></span>.
[e]<em>lit:</em> &ldquo;(I&rsquo;ve) lost it from me.&rdquo;
[e]&ldquo;I don&rsquo;t have it.&rdquo;[/d]
With similarity again to the dative verbs,  an animate destination may be swapped with the patient, <em>i.e.:</em> with the <strong>dative</strong> becoming an <strong>object</strong> and vice versa.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>&#x294;usu kalu kuffa fu.</strong>

[2]Apparent Verbs
These act like the transitive counterpart of the <a href="intransitivity.html#adjectivalverbs">adjectival</a> verbs, <em>i.e.:</em> the patient as the <strong>subject</strong>, the cause in <strong>ablative</strong> and the experiencer in <strong>dative</strong>. The additional <strong>object</strong>, which makes these transitive, is an abstract noun that refers to a quality or attribute, or an inanimate noun that refers to an actual substance or energy being released. The precise verb is chosen by whether the &lsquo;radiation&rsquo; is physical or <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/subtle.html#highlulani">subtle</a> in nature.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Hifumari ba&rsquo;u xi huba ra&rsquo;u?</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.HvmR / bu / X / Vb / ru.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hifu.html#highlulani">Hifu</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mari.html#highlulani">mari</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/ba'u.html#highlulani">ba&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xi.html#highlulani">xi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/huba.html#highlulani">huba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a>?
[e]<em>House-this</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2dat</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person dative</span></span> <em>seem important</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span>?
[e]&ldquo;Does this house seem important to you?&rdquo;[/d]
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Musa xu sa&rsquo;i.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.Us / Z / si.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/musa.html#highlulani">Musa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xu.html#highlulani">xu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sa'i.html#highlulani">sa&rsquo;i</a>.
[e]<em>Sun radiate light</em>.
[e]&ldquo;The sun is shining.&rdquo;[/d]
These verbs can also be used to signify the patients resemblance to something else. In this case, the other item or person is governed by the adposition <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ka.html#highlulani">ka</a> <high-lulani>k</high-lulani> <em>as.</em>
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Filli ka&rsquo;aggami xu. / Filli ka&rsquo;aggami xi.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.F;L / ka;gM / X.F;L / ka;gM / Z.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/filli.html#highlulani">Filli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ka.html#highlulani">ka</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'aggami.html#highlulani">&rsquo;aggami</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xu.html#highlulani">xu</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/filli.html#highlulani">Filli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ka.html#highlulani">ka</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'aggami.html#highlulani">&rsquo;aggami</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xi.html#highlulani">xi</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person intransitive</span></span> <em>as-police_officer appear</em>. / <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person intransitive</span></span> <em>as-police_officer seem</em>.

[2]Vital Verbs
These verbs require that both their <strong>objects</strong> and <strong>subjects</strong> are animate.

[2]Action Verbs
These verbs take an activity as an <strong>object</strong>. These can take the form of pure nouns:
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Hisutuba tara sinna.</strong>

[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hisutuba.html#highlulani">hisutuba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tara.html#highlulani">tara</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sinna.html#highlulani">sinna</a>.
[e]<em>Babysitter begin story</em>.
[e]&ldquo;The babysitter started the story.&rdquo;
[/d]
They can also take <a href="../../syntax/gerunds.html">gerunds</a>:
[d folding]

[1]Ambitransitivity
Ambitransitive verbs can be used with or without an argument in the object position.
[2]Perceptive Verbs
These verbs deal with the subject&rsquo;s ability to perceive stimuli.
When used purely intransitively, <em>i.e.: </em>with no direct or dative object, they refer to a general ability to use that sense:
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Guli ruku &rsquo;usa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.&lt;L / w&gt; / us.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/guli.html#highlulani">Guli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ruku.html#highlulani">ruku</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a>.
[e]<em>Blind_person</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>fut;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">future gnomic</span></span> <em>see</em>.
[e]&ldquo;The blind person can now see.&rdquo;
[/d]
When used with a direct <strong>object</strong>, this denotes a conscious effort at perception:
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Ju&rsquo;ipu&rsquo;a &rsquo;usa bumaki.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.Yioa / us / OmK.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ju'ipu'a.html#highlulani">Ju&rsquo;ipu&rsquo;a</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/bumaki.html#highlulani">bumaki</a>.
[e]<em>Assembly see screen.</em>
[e]&ldquo;The audience watched the screen.&rdquo;[/d]
When used with a <strong>dative</strong> object, this instead lacks that effort:
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Mihu kulasidaxi ju&rsquo;isataduru &rsquo;usa.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.MV / &gt;lSdX / YistEw / us.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku-lasida.html#highlulani">ku-lasida</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xi.html#highlulani">xi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ju'isatadu-ru.html#highlulani">ju&rsquo;isatadu-ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ani;int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">animate third person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>dat</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">dative</span></span>-<em>secret-seem conversation-</em><span class="tooltip"><small-caps>ger</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">gerund</span></span> <em>see</em>.
[e]&ldquo;She saw the secret meeting.&rdquo;[/d]

[2]Communicative Verbs
The communication itself is the <strong>object</strong>, and the recipient is <strong>dative</strong>.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Kimilli kul&middot;lani &rsquo;i &rsquo;issi.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.KM;L / &gt;WlN / i / i;S.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">Kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku-.html#highlulani">ku-</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'i.html#highlulani">&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'issi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;issi</a>.
[e]<em>King</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>dat</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">dative</span></span>-<em>song speak queen</em>
[e]&ldquo;The king sang to the queen.&rdquo;[/d]
Indirect speech is signified by a <a href="../../syntax/dependentclauses.html#contentclauses">complement</a> <strong>object</strong>.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Kimilli jusi &rsquo;i li lu&rsquo;i lulani ru</strong>.
[e]<high-lulani>.KM;L / &gt;L / Wi / WlN / w / i / MV.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">Kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/jusi.html#highlulani">jusi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'i.html#highlulani">&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/li.html#highlulani">li</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a>.
[e]<em>King</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ani;dat</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">animate third person dative</span></span> <em>speak</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>com</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">complementiser</span></span> <em>love queen</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present gnomic</span></span>.
[e]&ldquo;The king told him he loved the queen.&rdquo;[/d]
Directly reported communication is separated from the main clause by a comma, and may be put on either side. In this case, the recipient may be in either the <strong>object</strong> position or <strong>dative</strong>. This argument structure can also be used without a specific communication.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>(Mica,) kimilli &rsquo;i lulani.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.Mc , KM;L / i / WlN.</high-lulani>
[e](<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mica.html#highlulani">Mica</a>,) <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'i.html#highlulani">&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a>.
[e](<em>Hello,) king speak queen.</em>
[e]&ldquo;The king said &lsquo;hello&rsquo; / spoke to the queen.&rdquo;[/d]
[d wordlist]
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'i.html#highlulani">&rsquo;i</a> <high-lulani>i</high-lulani> <em>to speak</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/buma.html#highlulani">buma</a> <high-lulani>Om</high-lulani> <em>to draw</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a> <high-lulani>p</high-lulani> <em>to think</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/ma.html#highlulani">ma</a> <high-lulani>m</high-lulani> <em>to consider</em>[/d]
&date=20180403--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Auxiliaries
Auxiliaries are a type of <a href="verbs.html">verb</a>, however, they are sufficiently different from main verbs for them to be treated separately in this grammar. They are used to mark tense (the time at which an action takes place) and aspect (the nature of the passage of time during the action). The auxiliary can be dropped from a sentence if it is obvious from context, or is the same as that of the sentence immediately prior. They are a closed class.
[t]|h dynamic |h stative |h negative |h habitual |h gnomic
h past | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qilu.html#highlulani">qilu</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/taku.html#highlulani">taku</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/rusa.html#highlulani">rusa</a>
h present | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cani.html#highlulani">cani</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ji.html#highlulani">ji</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/na.html#highlulani">na</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a>

[/t]

Auxiliary stacking gives a poetic or archaic nuance.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>&#x294;usu rusarukuru lu&rsquo;i fu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.uz / wsw&gt;w / Wi / v.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&#x294;usu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/rusa.html#highlulani">rusa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ruku.html#highlulani">ruku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">fu</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person intransitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past gnomic</span></span>-<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>fut;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">future gnomic</span></span>-<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present gnomic</span></span> <em>love</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person transitive</span></span>.
[e]&ldquo;I have always and will always love you.&rdquo;
[/d]
[2]Tense
The three tenses are past, present and future. In conversation, the tenses tend to mark the time at which the action began or occurred.
On the other hand, narratives are mainly told in present tense. The other tenses are then used relatively, so that past tense is used for things that happened earlier than the narrative present, and the future tense for things that happened later.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Quhu qixa dasi si&rsquo;apa pada, jimuli cani janni qu, lanu haruqikanni la kiluqu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.AV / Qx / dS / Sap / pd , JUL / cN / j;N / A , lI / hwQk;N / l / KWA.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/quhu.html#highlulani">Quhu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/si'apa.html#highlulani">si&rsquo;apa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pada.html#highlulani">pada</a>, <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/jimuli.html#highlulani">jimuli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cani.html#highlulani">cani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qu.html#highlulani">qu</a>, <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lanu.html#highlulani">lanu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/haru.html#highlulani">haru</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qikanni.html#highlulani">qikanni</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/la.html#highlulani">la</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kiluqu.html#highlulani">kiluqu</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>3ani;tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">animate third person transitive</span></span> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;dyn</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past dynamic</span></span> <em>eat meal and_then, outside</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;dyn</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present dynamic</span></span> <em>move and,</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>fut;dyn</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">future dynamic</span></span> <em>with-dog do walk.</em>
[e]<em>lit.:</em> She did eat the meal, and then is going outside, and will do a walk with a dog.
[e]&ldquo;She ate the meal, went outside and walked the dog.&rdquo;
[/d]
[2]Aspect
The aspects of positive polarity can be categorised in two different ways. Each of these has two possibilities, and thus there are four altogether:
[t]|h episodic |h generic
h activity | dynamic | habitual
h state | stative | gnomic
[/t]
[d mobile-table]
<strong>activity</strong>:
[e]<strong>episodic</strong>: <em>dynamic</em>
[e]<strong>generic</strong>: <em>habitual</em>
<strong>state:</strong>
[e]<strong>episodic</strong>: <em>stative</em>
[e]<strong>generic</strong>: <em>gnomic</em>
[/d]
There is a single category of auxiliaries with the opposite polarity &mdash; the <strong>negative</strong>.
[3]Episodic and Generic
The difference between episodic and generic markers is one of extent. Events in <strong>episodic</strong> sentences take place over a finite duration; generic ones are prototypically unbounded, although this doesn&rsquo;t literally have to cover all of time.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Pannaxa cani &rsquo;ibibu.</strong> / <strong>Pannaxa na &rsquo;ibibu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.p;nx / n / iBO .p;nx / cN / iBO   </high-lulani><strong>.</strong>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pannaxa.html#highlulani">Pannaxa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cani.html#highlulani">cani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'ibibu.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ibibu</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pannaxa.html#highlulani">Pannaxa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/na.html#highlulani">na</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'ibibu.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ibibu</a>.
[e]<em>Warrior</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;dyn</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present dynamic</span></span> <em>complain</em>. / <em>Warrior</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;hab</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present habitual</span></span><em> complain.</em>
[e]Episodic: &ldquo;The warrior is complaining now.&rdquo; / Generic: &ldquo;The warrior always complains.&rdquo;
[/d]
[3]Activity <em>versus</em> State
The difference between activity and state for most verbs is one of focus, <em>ie.:</em> emphasis can be placed on the event itself (<strong>activity</strong>), or on the results (<strong>state</strong>).
[d folding]
[f]<strong>&#x294;a&rsquo;ima cani duci sunu.</strong> / <strong>&#x294;a&rsquo;ima pi duci sunu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.aim / P / EC / zI. aim / Qx / EC / zI.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'a'ima.html#highlulani">&#x294;a&rsquo;ima</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/duci.html#highlulani">duci</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sunu.html#highlulani">sunu</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'a'ima.html#highlulani">&#x294;a&rsquo;ima</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/duci.html#highlulani">duci</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sunu.html#highlulani">sunu</a>.
[e]<em>Traveller</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;dyn</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past dynamic</span></span><em> possess</em> <em>cloak.</em> / <em>Traveller</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past stative</span></span> <em>possess cloak.</em>
[e]Activity: &ldquo;The traveller gained a cloak.&rdquo; / State: &ldquo;The traveller owned a cloak.&rdquo;
[/d]
Perceptive verbs are treated slightly differently. Here, dynamic and habitual markers act as normal, however, the stative and gnomic are used to denote an ability to perceive a stimulus.
[d folding]
[f]<strong>Fu &rsquo;usa gufu&rsquo;iribuma cani?</strong> / <strong>Filli &rsquo;usa gufu&rsquo;iribuma ra&rsquo;u?</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>. F;L / us / &lt;viROm / ru . v / us / &lt;viROm / cN.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">Fu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gufu'iribuma.html#highlulani">gufu&rsquo;iribuma</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cani.html#highlulani">cani</a>? / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/filli.html#highlulani">Filli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gufu'iribuma.html#highlulani">gufu&rsquo;iribuma</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a>?
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person transitive</span></span> <em>see television</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;dyn</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present dynamic</span></span>? / <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person intransitive</span></span> <em>see television</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span>?
[e]Activity: &ldquo;Are you watching the TV?&rdquo; / State: &ldquo;Can you see the TV?&rdquo;
[/d]
[3]Negative
The negative aspect is used for actions, attributes and perceptions which do not occur. These act as the negation of any other aspectual marker. That is, while positive sentences can be classified by aspect, negative sentences all use the same auxiliaries.
&date=20180323--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Adverbs
Adverbs are a closed class. Adverbs can be used either as a verbal suffix or independently to describe the entire utterance. See Also: <a href="../syntax/adverbialphrases.html">Adverbial Phrases</a>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/naru.html#highlulani">naru</a> <em>slowly</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dura.html#highlulani">dura</a> <em>repeatedly</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kupira.html#highlulani">kupira</a> <em>intensely</em>
[2]Modals
A subclass of adverb are the modals, words used to denote properties of sentences, such as their reality, probability or the speaker&rsquo;s emotions towards the topic. These may only be used independently.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/matta.html#highlulani">matta</a> <em>again</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tasi.html#highlulani">tasi</a> <em>probably</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nufira.html#highlulani">nufira</a> <em>hopefully</em>
[3]Temporal Modals
Some modals dealing with time are zero-derived from abstract nouns.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/musa.html#highlulani">musa</a> <em>today</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/laru.html#highlulani">laru</a> <em>this year</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tariti.html#highlulani">tariti</a> <em>at noon</em>
Numbers can be suffixed to denote other times.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/musa.html#highlulani">musa</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hha.html#highlulani">hha</a> <em>yesterday (day 0</em>)
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/musa.html#highlulani">musa</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a> <em>tomorrow (day 2</em>)
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/laru.html#highlulani">laru</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mullu.html#highlulani">mullu</a> <em>two years ago (year <overline>1</overline></em>)

[1]Deixis
[2]Topicality
Once a topic is introduced in a discourse or narrative, it can be assumed to be the subject until changed.
[2]Indefinite Pro-forms
The indefinite pro-forms are sets of deictic words which can be placed into a table.
