[e]action: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'amila.html#highlulani">&rsquo;amila</a>
[e]manner / state: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fana.html#highlulani">fana</a>
[/d]
Proximate forms have referents physically or psychologically near the speaker, whereas distal forms are used when the referent is far away. Interrogative forms are used in questions, and negative forms are used in negative sentences. Universal means &ldquo;all&rdquo; or &ldquo;every&rdquo;, and existential means &ldquo;some&rdquo; or &ldquo;any&rdquo;.
[3]Indefinite Pronouns
Unlike some personal pronouns, indefinite pronouns are not marked for animacy.
The pronouns in the object column are used for people and things.
The place column pronouns are used for locations in both space and time.
The &lsquo;object&rsquo; indefinite pronouns can modify a noun when used as a suffix. When <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cu'i.html#highlulani">cu&rsquo;i</a> <em>nothing</em> is used as a suffix, it loses its last syllable. When <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'umi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;umi</a> <em>something</em> is used as a suffix, it loses its first syllable.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/taka.html#highlulani">taka</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cu.html#highlulani">cu</a> <em>no sound</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/manafa.html#highlulani">manafa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mari.html#highlulani">mari</a> <em>this country</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mi.html#highlulani">mi</a> <em>some monarch</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kulu.html#highlulani">kulu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'aba.html#highlulani">&rsquo;aba</a> <em>every fork</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nulli.html#highlulani">nulli</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sama.html#highlulani">sama</a> <em>which mountain?</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&#x294;usu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'aba.html#highlulani">&rsquo;aba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/filli.html#highlulani">filli</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'aba.html#highlulani">&rsquo;aba</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta.html#highlulani">ta</a> <em>every me and every you</em>
The existential markers are used in complements.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&#x294;usu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/li.html#highlulani">li</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xaha.html#highlulani">xaha</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/disi.html#highlulani">disi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'umi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;umi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/padissu.html#highlulani">padissu</a>.
[e]<em>1int com name-3ani;gen something prs;gno learn.</em>
[e]&ldquo;I learned what her name is.&rdquo;
The dative marker is not applied to distal pronouns.
Reduplicated indefinite pronouns with suffixed -<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta.html#highlulani">ta</a> <em>and</em> are used for emphasis.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sama.html#highlulani">sama</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sama.html#highlulani">sama</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta.html#highlulani">ta</a> <em>what the hell?</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cu'i.html#highlulani">cu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cu'i.html#highlulani">cu&rsquo;i</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta.html#highlulani">ta</a> <em>nothing and no one</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qa'i.html#highlulani">qa&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qa'i.html#highlulani">qa&rsquo;i</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta.html#highlulani">ta</a> <em>never ever</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'aba.html#highlulani">&rsquo;aba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'aba.html#highlulani">&rsquo;aba</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta.html#highlulani">ta</a> <em>absolutely everything</em>
[2]Pro-verbs
The action terms are pro-verbs, which can be used to replace ordinary verbs in sentences.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/filli.html#highlulani">Filli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sulla.html#highlulani">sulla</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a>?
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person intransitive</span></span><em> do_what pst;dyn?</em>
[e]&ldquo;What did you do?&rdquo;
[2]Pro-modals
The manner column is used to refer to the way in which an action is undertaken, and the state column refers to the condition of a thing. These are used as modal adverbs.
[2]Possessive Markers
An item possessed by the third-person subject of a matrix clause need not appear with a genitive marker, whether the possession is alienable or inalienable.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sabba.html#highlulani">Sabba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tu.html#highlulani">tu</a>.
[e]<em>Father see daughter.</em>
[e]&ldquo;Dad saw his daughter.&rdquo;
If a genitive marker does appear, it takes the form <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/su'a.html#highlulani">su&rsquo;a</a> <em>own</em>.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sabba.html#highlulani">Sabba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tu.html#highlulani">tu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/su'a.html#highlulani">su&rsquo;a</a>.
[e]<em>Father saw daughter-own.</em>
[e]&ldquo;Dad spoke to his daughter.&rdquo;
The usual genitive markers refer to possession by some other party, not the subject.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sabba.html#highlulani">Sabba</a>  <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tu.html#highlulani">tu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/li.html#highlulani">li</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ranini.html#highlulani">ranini</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/disi.html#highlulani">disi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lanu.html#highlulani">lanu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hiqa.html#highlulani">hiqa</a>.
[e]<em>Father offspring com eat potato-dim-3ani;gen fut;dyn order.</em>
[e]&ldquo;Dad asked his daughter to eat her chips.&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sabba.html#highlulani">Sabba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tu.html#highlulani">tu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/li.html#highlulani">li</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ranini.html#highlulani">ranini</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/su'a.html#highlulani">su&rsquo;a</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lanu.html#highlulani">lanu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hiqa.html#highlulani">hiqa</a>.
[e]<em>Father offspring com eat potato-dim-own fut;dyn order.</em>
[e]&ldquo;Dad asked my daughter to eat his chips.&rdquo;
None of the above applies for first- and second-person subjects; these use their normal genitive markers.
&date=20180327--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Suffixes
Suffixes can be used to derive new word from existing vocabulary. A suffix beginning with a vowel replaces the final vowel of the base.
[2]Derivational Suffixes
These derive words within a class, <em>i.e.:</em> a noun from a noun, or a verb from a verb.
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/-aku.html#highlulani">-aku</a> forms an augmentative. It is most often attached to nouns to reference something large or important. It is rarely used for people.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tissaku.html#highlulani">tissaku</a> <em>wind</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'isilaku.html#highlulani">&rsquo;isilaku</a> <em>depression</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-ini.html#highlulani">-ini</a> is used to form diminutives, words referencing something small or unimportant. When used with animate nouns, it creates a word for the young of non-sapient creatures. However, with sapient creatures, this word is obscene.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'ahatini.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ahatini</a> <em>contentment</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tissini.html#highlulani">tissini</a> <em>breeze</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qikannini.html#highlulani">qikannini</a> <em>puppy</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ranini.html#highlulani">ranini</a> <em>potato chips</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/bi'ini.html#highlulani">bi&rsquo;ini</a> <em>to itch</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/-fi.html#highlulani">-fi</a> confers a nuance of sacredness or honour upon a base word.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/karafi.html#highlulani">karafi</a> <em>sacredness</em>
[e]<strong>lulanifi</strong> <em>great queen</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/-tu'i.html#highlulani">-tu&rsquo;i</a> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/da.html#highlulani">da</a> are used to highlight the positive and negative aspects of a word, respectively.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasatu'i.html#highlulani">dasatu&rsquo;i</a> <em>passion</em> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasada.html#highlulani">dasada</a> <em>anger</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta'itu'i.html#highlulani">ta&rsquo;itu&rsquo;i</a> <em>aroma</em> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta'ida.html#highlulani">ta&rsquo;ida</a> <em>stink</em>
[3]Nominal suffixes
These derive nouns from other nouns.
[t] | Inanimate Base | Abstract Base
[r]Animate | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-rra.html#highlulani">-rra</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/-sa.html#highlulani">-sa</a> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-ri.html#highlulani">-ri</a>
[r]Inanimate |  | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/-di.html#highlulani">-di</a>
[r]Abstract | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/-ja.html#highlulani">-ja</a>[/t]
<div class="mobile-table">
inanimate
[e] &rarr; animate: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-rra.html#highlulani">-rra</a>
[e] &rarr; abstract: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/-ja.html#highlulani">-ja</a>
abstract
[e] &rarr; animate: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/-sa.html#highlulani">-sa</a> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-ri.html#highlulani">-ri</a>
[e] &rarr; inanimate: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/-di.html#highlulani">-di</a></div>
The above table shows the suffixes used for deriving nouns between different animacy classes.
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-rra.html#highlulani">-rra</a> derives an animate noun from an inanimate noun.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tisakarra.html#highlulani">tisakarra</a> <em>townsperson</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/-sa.html#highlulani">-sa</a> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-ri.html#highlulani">-ri</a> both derive an animate noun from an abstract noun, however, these are not predictable. For instance, note the difference between <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dis.sa.html#highlulani">dis&middot;sa</a> <em>youth</em> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dissuri.html#highlulani">dissuri</a> <em>stranger</em>. Other examples are:
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pucasa.html#highlulani">pucasa</a> <em>optimist</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sasa.html#highlulani">sasa</a> <em>introvert</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dattusa.html#highlulani">dattusa</a> <em>god</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulisa.html#highlulani">mulisa</a> <em>fool</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/luxirasa.html#highlulani">luxirasa</a> <em>twin</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tuhhisa.html#highlulani">tuhhisa</a> <em>farmer</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'axasiri.html#highlulani">&rsquo;axasiri</a> <em>adult</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'asilari.html#highlulani">&rsquo;asilari</a> <em>friend</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-ri.html#highlulani">-ri</a> also denotes people from a particular place.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tinalliri.html#highlulani">Tinalliri</a> <em>Tinellbian</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/-di.html#highlulani">-di</a> derives an inanimate noun from something abstract, and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/-ja.html#highlulani">-ja</a> does the opposite.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sinnadi.html#highlulani">sinnadi</a> <em>book</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru'ihaja.html#highlulani">ru&rsquo;ihaja</a> <em>history</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-kku.html#highlulani">-kku</a> derives the names of parts of the body from either a noun or a verb.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'itikku.html#highlulani">&rsquo;itikku</a> <em>breast</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulukku.html#highlulani">mulukku</a> <em>heart</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasikku.html#highlulani">dasikku</a> <em>digestive system</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/-mi.html#highlulani">-mi</a> denotes an animate giver of the inanimate or abstract base.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'aggami.html#highlulani">&rsquo;aggami</a> <em>police officer</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sa'imi.html#highlulani">Sa&rsquo;imi</a> <em>Caemi, giver of light</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/-qi.html#highlulani">-qi</a> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-kati.html#highlulani">-kati</a> denote the feminine and masculine respectively, however they are infrequently used.
[3]Verbal suffixes
These are only applied to verbs.
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/-ni.html#highlulani">-ni</a> derives an inceptive verb
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/ducini.html#highlulani">ducini</a> <em>to receive</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/-ulu.html#highlulani">-ulu</a> denotes reversal of an action.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulu.html#highlulani">lulu</a> <em>to undo</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/jannulu.html#highlulani">jannulu</a> <em>to return</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/turulu.html#highlulani">turulu</a> <em>to open</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ju'ulu.html#highlulani">ju&rsquo;ulu</a> <em>to unlink</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/-tuni.html#highlulani">-tuni</a> denotes repeat of an action.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/latuni.html#highlulani">latuni</a> <em>to do again</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/-ssasu.html#highlulani">-ssasu</a> is an augmentative used specifically for verbs.
[f]<strong>bi&rsquo;ussasu</strong> <em>to really hurt</em>
[3]Other Parts of Speech
These suffixes are applied to words other than nouns and verbs.
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/-ar-.html#highlulani">-ar-</a> is actually an infix, placed before the final vowel of auxiliaries, and denotes an end to the action described by the sentence.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lanaru.html#highlulani">lanaru</a> <em>will finish doing</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nagari.html#highlulani">nagari</a> <em>will finish being</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/-ma.html#highlulani">-ma</a> derives terminative adverbs.
[f]<strong>nufirama</strong> <em>no longer wanting</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/-hita.html#highlulani">-hita</a> is used to negate adverbs.
[f]<strong>nufirahita</strong> <em>not wanting</em>
[2]Nominalisation
These derive a noun from another part of speech, most often a verb. They are categorised here by the animacy class of the resultant word.
[3]Abstract
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/-'a.html#highlulani">-&rsquo;a</a> is a productive general suffix for deriving abstract nouns.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cura'a.html#highlulani">cura&rsquo;a</a> <em>time</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qacca'a.html#highlulani">qacca&rsquo;a</a> <em>choice</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa'a.html#highlulani">pa&rsquo;a</a> <em>thought</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/-ru.html#highlulani">-ru</a> forms gerunds.
[f]<strong>dasiru</strong> <em>eating</em>
[e]<strong>janniru</strong> <em>moving</em>
[e]<strong>hubaru</strong> <em>breathing</em>
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/-ppa.html#highlulani">-ppa</a> derives terms used for times and occasions.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasippa.html#highlulani">dasippa</a> <em>mealtime</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sikuppa.html#highlulani">sikuppa</a> <em>funeral</em>
[3]Inanimate
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/-du.html#highlulani">-du</a> derives a patientive inanimate noun from a verb.
[f]
-ffi: stem derivational suffix verb &rarr; noun instrument; tool
-kku: derivational suffix noun ; verb &rarr; noun body part
-ssiji: derivational suffix mathematics &rarr; noun derives the names of shapes from the number of edges or vertices
Animate
-la&rsquo;i: derivational suffix verb &rarr; noun derives an animate noun from an intransitive verb
-ba: derivational suffix verb &rarr; noun derives an animate agentive noun from a transitive verb
-pu&rsquo;a: derivational suffix verb &rarr; noun derives an animate patientive noun from a transitive verb
Any
-ahi: derivational suffix adverb &rarr; noun derives a noun from an adverb
-muka: derivational suffix adposition &rarr; noun derives a noun from a prepositional phrase
-qa: derivational suffix numeral verb pronoun &rarr; noun nominaliser; nmn
Other Part of Speech changes
-atinna: derivational suffix verb &rarr; adverb derives an adverb from a verb
-niqqi: derivational suffix noun &rarr; adverb derives an adverb from a noun
&date=20180403--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Adpositions
Adpositions are a closed class.
[2]Uses
Adpositions can be used in three different ways.
[3]Preposition
The most basic use for an adposition is prefixed to a noun to signify where the action is taking place with relation to a reference.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/di.html#highlulani">di</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'i'uja.html#highlulani">&rsquo;i&rsquo;uja</a> <em>atop the table</em> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/di.html#highlulani">di</a> <em>up</em> ; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'i'uja.html#highlulani">&rsquo;i&rsquo;uja</a> <em>table</em>)
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/haru.html#highlulani">haru</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a> <em>with the queen</em> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/haru.html#highlulani">haru</a> <em>with</em> ; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a> <em>queen</em>)
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/ni.html#highlulani">ni</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cula.html#highlulani">cula</a> <em>in an egg</em> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/ni.html#highlulani">ni</a> <em>at</em> ; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cula.html#highlulani">cula</a> <em>egg</em>)
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qa.html#highlulani">qa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu.html#highlulani">kalu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'ita'i.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ita&rsquo;i</a> <em>down from the cart</em> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qa.html#highlulani">qa</a> <em>down</em> ; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu.html#highlulani">kalu</a> <em>from</em> ; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'ita'i.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ita&rsquo;i</a> <em>cart</em>)
[3]Nominal and Verbal Modifier
Adpositions can also be used in conjunction with nouns and verbs to make compounds.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gibi.html#highlulani">gibi</a> <em>to go east</em> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a> <em>to move</em> ; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gibi.html#highlulani">gibi</a> <em>east</em>)
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gusu.html#highlulani">gusu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'adi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;adi</a> <em>nearby people</em> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gusu.html#highlulani">gusu</a> <em>person</em> ; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'adi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;adi</a> <em>near</em>)
[3]Adverb
Adpositions can be used by themselves to show the position of the action relative to the speaker, or the direction in which the action proceeds. Unlike other adverbs, these are placed after the auxiliary.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'adi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;adi</a> <em>nearby</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qa.html#highlulani">qa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hussu.html#highlulani">hussu</a> <em>drop down</em> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qa.html#highlulani">qa</a> <em>down</em> ; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hussu.html#highlulani">hussu</a> <em>drop</em>)
[2]List
[3]Cardinal Directions
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ka.html#highlulani">ka</a> <em>south</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sumika.html#highlulani">sumika</a> <em>west</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sani.html#highlulani">sani</a> <em>north</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gibi.html#highlulani">gibi</a> <em>east</em>
[3]Locations
These can be used to refer to locations in either space or time
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'adi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;adi</a> <em>near; now</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xidu.html#highlulani">xidu</a> <em>far</em>

[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qa.html#highlulani">qa</a> <em>down; below; beneath; after</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'ari.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ari</a> <em>front; before</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/capi.html#highlulani">capi</a> <em>behind; after</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a> <em>towards; at</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/ni.html#highlulani">ni</a> <em>at; in; during</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kika.html#highlulani">kika</a> <em>over</em>
[3]Spatial Locations
These can only be used to refer to locations in space.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/jimuli.html#highlulani">jimuli</a> <em>outside</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qu'u.html#highlulani">qu&rsquo;u</a> <em>in; inside</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nifi.html#highlulani">nifi</a> <em>next to; beside; besides</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/raqu.html#highlulani">raqu</a> <em>between; among</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/ca.html#highlulani">ca</a> <em>encircling</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/du'i.html#highlulani">du&rsquo;i</a> <em>beyond; opposite</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/la'a.html#highlulani">la&rsquo;a</a> <em>on a horizontal surface</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kadu.html#highlulani">kadu</a> <em>on a vertical surface</em>
[3]Motion
These refer to motion
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/data.html#highlulani">data</a> <em>backwards</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tirri.html#highlulani">tirri</a> <em>forwards</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ja.html#highlulani">ja</a> <em>along</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/ma'iki.html#highlulani">ma&rsquo;iki</a> <em>across</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tiku.html#highlulani">tiku</a> <em>around</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/bi.html#highlulani">bi</a> <em>out; out of; from</em>
[3]Animates
This group have animate objects.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/haru.html#highlulani">haru</a> <em>with</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/ha.html#highlulani">ha</a> <em>for the benefit of</em>
[3]Inanimates
This group have inanimate objects.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nidu.html#highlulani">nidu</a> <em>with; using</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sarru.html#highlulani">sarru</a> <em>without; instead of; rather than</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/haru.html#highlulani">haru</a> <em>consisting of</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nina.html#highlulani">nina</a> <em>used for a purpose</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sata.html#highlulani">sata</a> <em>in order to obtain</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'arri.html#highlulani">&rsquo;arri</a> <em>along with</em>
&date=20170725
--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Determiners
A determiner can be used to narrow the reference of a noun. They can only be used as noun suffixes.
[2]List
[3]Quantity
These are used to answer &rdquo;how many?&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cu.html#highlulani">cu</a> <em>no; zero</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mimu'i.html#highlulani">mimu&rsquo;i</a> <em>some; more than one</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lumi.html#highlulani">lumi</a> <em>several</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'uhu.html#highlulani">&rsquo;uhu</a> <em>many</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> <em>many</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/raqi.html#highlulani">raqi</a> <em>more; additional</em>
[3]Choice
There are two sets of determiners, both used to select a part from the whole. One group is used with count nouns, the other with mass nouns.
[4]Count Nouns
These refer to particular members of a group.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cu.html#highlulani">cu</a> <em>none</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sama.html#highlulani">sama</a> <em>which</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/ca.html#highlulani">ca</a> <em>only</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fi'atu.html#highlulani">fi&rsquo;atu</a> <em>certain; particular</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mi.html#highlulani">mi</a> <em>any; some</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tapa.html#highlulani">tapa</a> <em>next</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cari.html#highlulani">cari</a> <em>remaining; rest</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qafa.html#highlulani">qafa</a> <em>last; final</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'aba.html#highlulani">&rsquo;aba</a> <em>all</em>
[4]Mass Nouns
These refer to sections of a substance.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cari.html#highlulani">cari</a> <em>remaining; rest</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sukki.html#highlulani">sukki</a> <em>entire; whole; all</em>
[3]Directional
These refer to particular objects, based on their direction.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mari.html#highlulani">mari</a> <em>this</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kasi.html#highlulani">kasi</a> <em>that</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gi.html#highlulani">gi</a> <em>left; on the left-hand side</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/saqa.html#highlulani">saqa</a> <em>right; on the right-hand side</em>
[3]Degree
These mark the degree to which the noun matches its referent.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ji'a.html#highlulani">ji&rsquo;a</a> <em>not; not a</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/naci.html#highlulani">naci</a> <em>somewhat</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nata.html#highlulani">nata</a> <em>complete; utter</em>
[3]Miscellaneous
This last terms do not fit into any of the other categories.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cama.html#highlulani">cama</a> <em>usual; old; familiar; customary</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nisa.html#highlulani">nisa</a> <em>only; sole; one</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/li.html#highlulani">li</a> <em>other</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sabufi.html#highlulani">sabufi</a> <em>different</em>
&date=20170726
--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Particles
There are very few particles. These are simply words that do not fit neatly into any other category.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/li.html#highlulani">li</a> <em>complementiser</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xiku.html#highlulani">xiku</a> <em>relativiser</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/piba.html#highlulani">piba</a> <em>superlative</em>
&date=20170716
--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Conjunctions
Conjunctions are a closed class of words which are used to join phrases or clauses together.
[2]Phrase-level Conjunctions
These conjunctions are used to join words or phrases. They are enclitics.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/ta.html#highlulani">ta</a> <em>and</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sija.html#highlulani">sija</a> <em>or</em>
[2]Clause-level Conjunctions
These conjunctions are used to join clauses or sentences. They are used as independent words.
[3]Coordinating Conjunctions
Coordinating conjunctions are used to separate two matrix clauses. They are placed at the beginning of the second clause.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qu.html#highlulani">qu</a> <em>and</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nuki.html#highlulani">nuki</a> <em>or</em>
[3]Subordinating Conjunctions
Subordinating conjunctions are used to introduce a dependent clause.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/surra.html#highlulani">surra</a> <em>when</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/daru'i.html#highlulani">daru&rsquo;i</a> <em>because</em>
&date=20170725
--------------------------------------------------2
[1]Syntax
High Lulani is head-initial in compounds, but tends to be head-final in phrases and clauses. The language has Subject-Verb-Object order, but shows signs of an SOV nature, as dative and ablative complements become more common.
&date=20180223--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Case
[2]Alignment
The three basic arguments for any verb (intransitive subjects, transitive subjects and transitive objects) are marked in High Lulani. Because intransitive subjects cannot co-occur with transitive arguments, it is possible to mark either of the transitive arguments in the same way as the intransitive without confusion. In the ergative alignment, it is the transitive object that is marked the same as the intransitive subject. In accusative alignment, it is instead the transitive subject that shares marking with intransitive subjects. In either alignment, the intransitive case is the one treated like the intransitive subject, and the transitive case is the other.
High Lulani has an ergativity split, made down aspectual lines. A clause using dynamic or iterative auxiliaries uses ergative alignment; gnomic, stative and negative aspects attract the accusative.
[2]Core Cases
The core cases mark the basic arguments of the verb. Common or proper nouns have no case markings for these, but the pronouns have different forms. Therefore only pronouns show the alignment of a sentence.
[3]Intransitive
The intransitive case is used for the sole argument of an intransitive verb and for the unmarked argument of transitive sentences. This case is also used for adpositions.
[3]Transitive
The transitive case is used for the marked argument of transitive sentences, that is, the object in an accusative clause, and the subject in ergative clauses.
[2]Oblique Cases
The two oblique cases are marked on the pronouns. For common and proper nouns, a clitic with the same form as the appropriate third person inanimate pronoun is placed before the noun phrase.
Sometimes the verb requires an oblique rather than a traditional object. In these cases, the subject is usually in intransitive case, although it is not incorrect to use transitive case with dynamic and iterative auxiliaries.
[3]Ablative
The ablative case is used to mark the proximate cause or the instigator of an action. With verbs of transfer or motion, it is also used to mark the source of a movement. The clitic is <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu.html#highlulani">kalu</a>.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sacu.html#highlulani">sacu</a> because of you / from you
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu.html#highlulani">kalu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tinalli.html#highlulani">Tinalli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a> come from Tinellb (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a> to move)
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu.html#highlulani">kalu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kuffa.html#highlulani">kuffa</a> given by the king (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">kimilli</a> king ; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kuffa.html#highlulani">kuffa</a> to give)
[3]Dative
The dative case was originally only used to mark the receiver with verbs of giving and transfer. The meaning has since broadened to show indirectness on the part of the patient for a number of verbs, including verbs of perception and emotion. The clitic is <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku.html#highlulani">ku</a>.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pixi.html#highlulani">pixi</a> to me
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/jusi.html#highlulani">jusi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a> to see him (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/jusi.html#highlulani">jusi</a> to him ; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a> <em>see</em>)
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku.html#highlulani">ku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'irri'a.html#highlulani">&#x294;irri&rsquo;a</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a> go to Ir&igrave;a (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/janni.html#highlulani">janni</a> <em>to move</em>)
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku.html#highlulani">ku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kuffa.html#highlulani">kuffa</a> give to the queen (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a> queen ; <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kuffa.html#highlulani">kuffa</a> to give)
&date=20170725
--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Matrix Clauses
The standard word order for matrix clauses is:
Subject &dash; Auxiliary &dash; Adposition - Oblique &dash; Verb &dash; Object &dash; Adverb.
None of these slots are compulsorily filled. If a subject is obvious from context, or is the same as that of the immediately prior sentence, it can be dropped. The adverb can act as a pro-sentence.
[2]Intransitive Clauses
As already discussed, intransitive clauses do not have objects.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nara.html#highlulani">nara</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3int</small-caps> <small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps> <em>sleep</em>
[e]&ldquo;He is asleep.&rdquo;
[2]Transitive Clauses
Transitive clauses do require an object.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&#x294;usu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">fu</a>.
[e]<small-caps>1int</small-caps> <small-caps>prs;gno</small-caps> <em>love</em><small-caps>2tra</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;I love you.&rdquo;
Sometimes the object is in an oblique case.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku.html#highlulani">ku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qikanni.html#highlulani">qikanni</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usa</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3ani;int</small-caps> <small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps> <small-caps>dat</small-caps><em>-dog see</em>.
[e]&ldquo;She can see the dog.&rdquo;
[2]Copular Sentences
Copular sentences do not have a main verb. These sentences are used to show an equivalence relationship between two nouns, or to show that one noun is an element of the set described by the other noun. They are transitive sentences.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lanu.html#highlulani">lanu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/julliga.html#highlulani">julliga</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3ani;int</small-caps> <small-caps>fut;dyn</small-caps> <em>married_woman</em>
[e]&ldquo;She will become a married woman.&rdquo;
Another use of copular sentences is to tell the location of something in relation to something else.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">Pa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/di.html#highlulani">di</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'i'uja.html#highlulani">&rsquo;i&rsquo;uja</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3ina;int</small-caps> <small-caps>prs;gno</small-caps> <em>down-table</em>
[e]&ldquo;It&rsquo;s under the table.&rdquo;
The copular sentence structure for ownership is as follows. It has the possessor in the dative case, and the possessum as the subject.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sunu.html#highlulani">Sunu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pixi.html#highlulani">pixi</a>.
[e]<em>Cloak</em> <small-caps>prs;gno 1dat</small-caps>
[e]I have a cloak.
The arguments may be swapped without a change in meaning.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pixi.html#highlulani">Pixi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sunu.html#highlulani">sunu</a>.
[e]<em><small-caps>1dat prs;gno</small-caps> cloak.</em>
[e]I have a cloak.
[2]Contrasting Pronouns
These example sentences have been given to clarify alignment and the correct use of pronouns with different auxiliaries.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3ani.int pst;dyn</small-caps> <em>red</em>
[e]&ldquo;She turned red.&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3ani.int pst;sta</small-caps> <em>red</em>
[e]&ldquo;She was red.&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/quhu.html#highlulani">Quhu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3ani.tra pst;dyn</small-caps> <em>eat</em><small-caps> 3ina.int</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;She ate it.&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">Mihu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'iffa.html#highlulani">&rsquo;iffa</a>.
[e]<small-caps>3ani.int pst;sta</small-caps> <em>eat</em><small-caps> 3ina.tra</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;She was eating it.&rdquo;
As can be seen, the only time the transitive case is used for the subject of a clause is in transitive (as well as copular) sentences using dynamic or iterative auxiliaries.
&date=20170730
--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Argument Promotion
The first noun in a clause is the subject, which is prototypically the agent in transitive sentences and the patient in intransitive sentences. However, suffixes can be added to the verb to promote other nouns in the clause, other than the genitive.
There are three such verbal suffixes, which can be stacked, however, once something has been shifted from the subject position, it can&rsquo;t be promoted again.
[2]Passive
The passive suffix promotes the object. This suffix has the form <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-'illu.html#highlulani">-&rsquo;illu</a> when the last element of a verb is monosyllabic, has <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-ilu.html#highlulani">-ilu</a> replacing the final vowel if the final consonant is geminated, and has <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-illu.html#highlulani">-illu</a> replacing the final vowel of the verb elsewise. The old subject is then marked with the ablative case. A sentence with this marker is intransitive. The demoted item is not compulsory, but if it is put in, it is the first ablative-marked noun in the new sentence.
[f]<strong>Fu qixa kissa kilatu&rsquo;i!</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.v / Qx / K;s / Klei.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">Fu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kissa.html#highlulani">kissa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kilatu'i.html#highlulani">kilatu&rsquo;i</a>!
[e]<small-caps>2tra pst;dyn</small-caps> <em>fight deer</em>
[e]&ldquo;You fought a deer!&rdquo;
[f]<strong>Kilatu&rsquo;i qixa (sacu) kissilu.</strong>
[e]<high-lulani>.Klei / Qx / sy / K;SW.</high-lulani>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kilatu'i.html#highlulani">Kilatu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sacu.html#highlulani">sacu</a>) <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kissa.html#highlulani">kissa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-ilu.html#highlulani">-ilu</a>.
[e]<em>deer</em> <small-caps>pst;dyn (2abl)</small-caps> <em>fight</em><small-caps>-psv</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;A deer was fought (by you).&rdquo;
[2]Ablative
When the final consonant of a verb is geminate, the ablative suffix takes the form <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-ka.html#highlulani">-ka</a>, elsewise it is <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-kka.html#highlulani">-kka</a>. The old subject is demoted to object, and the old object is demoted to dative. A sentence with this marker is transitive. The first dative-marked noun in the new sentence is the demoted item.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">Lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu.html#highlulani">kalu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qasa.html#highlulani">qasa</a>.
[e]<em>queen</em><small-caps> pst;dyn abl-</small-caps><em>king</em><small-caps></small-caps> <em>eat</em><small-caps></small-caps> <em>fish</em>
[e]&ldquo;The queen ate a fish because of the king.&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">Kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku.html#highlulani">ku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qasa.html#highlulani">qasa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasikka.html#highlulani">dasikka</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a>.
[e]<em>king</em><small-caps> pst;dyn dat-</small-caps><em>fish</em><small-caps></small-caps> <em>eat</em><small-caps>-abp</small-caps> <em>queen</em><small-caps>.</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;The king made the queen eat fish.&rdquo;
[f]<strong>Kimilli qixa (kal&middot;lani) dasilluka qasa.</strong>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">Kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu.html#highlulani">kalu</a>-<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dasi.html#highlulani">dasi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/-illu.html#highlulani">-illu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/-ka.html#highlulani">-ka</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qasa.html#highlulani">qasa</a>.
[e]<em>king</em> <small-caps>pst;dyn</small-caps> (abl-</small-caps><em>queen</em><small-caps>)</small-caps> <em>eat</em><small-caps>-psv-abp</small-caps> <em>fish</em>
[e]&ldquo;The king made the fish get eaten (by the queen).&rdquo;
[2]Dative
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xa.html#highlulani">xa</a> promotes a dative. The old subject is demoted to object, and the old object (if any) is demoted to dative. A sentence with this marker is transitive.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulisa.html#highlulani">Mulisa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku.html#highlulani">ku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/quxi.html#highlulani">quxi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kuffa.html#highlulani">kuffa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/laqqu.html#highlulani">laqqu</a>.
[e]<em>fool</em> <small-caps>prs;gno dat</small-caps>-<em>mountain give money</em>.
[e]&ldquo;A fool gives money to the mountain.&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/quxi.html#highlulani">Quxi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku.html#highlulani">ku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/laqqu.html#highlulani">laqqu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kuffa.html#highlulani">kuffa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xa.html#highlulani">xa</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulisa.html#highlulani">mulisa</a>.
[e]<em>mountain</em><small-caps> prs;gno dat-</small-caps><em>money</em><small-caps> give-dtv</small-caps> <em>fool</em>
[e]&ldquo;It is to the mountain that fools give money.&rdquo;

[2]Adposition
To promote a adpositional phrase to subject, prefix the verb with the adposition. The old subject is demoted to object. The old object, if any, is demoted to dative.

[1]Dependent Clauses
A dependent clause is a clause that is unable to stand meaningfully by itself.
They are marked by having the auxiliary at the end.
[2]Subordinate Clauses
A subordinate clause is one introduced by a subordinating conjunction in the matrix clause. A comma is used to separate a subordinate from its matrix. The conjunction is placed on the side of the main clause that is closest to the subordinate. The clauses can be put in either order.
[f]<strong>&#x294;usu ru lu&rsquo;i fu daru&rsquo;i, <u>ba pu&rsquo;iba miku ra&rsquo;u</u>.</strong>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&#x294;usu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">fu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/daru'i.html#highlulani">daru&rsquo;i</a>, <u><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/ba.html#highlulani">ba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pu'iba.html#highlulani">pu&rsquo;iba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a></u>.
[e]<small-caps>1int prs;gno</small-caps> <em>love</em><small-caps> 2tra</small-caps> <em>because</em><small-caps>, 2gen</small-caps> <em>ball</em><small-caps></small-caps> <em>red</em><small-caps> prs;sta</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;I love you because your ball is red.&rdquo;
[f]<strong><u>Ba pu&rsquo;iba miku ra&rsquo;u</u>, daru&rsquo;i &rsquo;usu ru lu&rsquo;i fu.</strong>
[e]<u><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/ba.html#highlulani">Ba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pu'iba.html#highlulani">pu&rsquo;iba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a></u>, <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/daru'i.html#highlulani">daru&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">fu</a>.

[e]&ldquo;I love you because your ball is red.&rdquo;
Here the subordinate clauses are underlined. The cause is subordinate to the effect.
[2]Adverbial Clauses
An adverbial clause is one which acts as an adverb.
[3]Location Adverbial Clauses
The word <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/ma.html#highlulani">ma</a> <em>where</em> is often used as a prefix for adpositions used as clausal conjunctions.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usu.html#highlulani">&#x294;usu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">fu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/madi.html#highlulani">madi</a>, <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/ba.html#highlulani">ba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pu'iba.html#highlulani">pu&rsquo;iba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qixa.html#highlulani">qixa</a>.
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>1int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">first person intransitive</span></span> <em>love</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person transitive</span></span> <em>where-up,</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2gen</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person genitive</span></span> <em>ball red</em> <small-caps>pst;dyn.</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;I loved you before your ball turned red.&rdquo;
[2]Content Clauses
A content clause is one that takes the place of a noun. They begin with the complementiser <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/li.html#highlulani">li</a> and are separated from the matrix clause by commas. The auxiliary is not optional, and is given a low tone. Quote marks are used around reported speech, replacing the complementiser.

[2]Relative Clauses
Relative clauses specify the noun by describing it. They are placed before the modified noun, beginning with the relativiser <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xiku.html#highlulani">xiku</a>. The auxiliary is not optional, and is given a rising tone. Only subjects can be relativised. Other cases must be promoted to subject.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xiku.html#highlulani">Xiku</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a>.
[e]<small-caps>rel</small-caps> <em>love king</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past stative</span></span> <em>queen</em>
[e]&ldquo;The queen who loved the king.&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xiku.html#highlulani">Xiku</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu.html#highlulani">kalu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'illu.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;illu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a>.
[e]<small-caps>rel</small-caps> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>abl</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">ablative</span></span><em>-king love-</em><small-caps>psv</small-caps> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past stative</span></span> <em>queen</em>
[e]&ldquo;The queen whom the king loved.&rdquo;
Any noun can be modified by relative clauses, including pronouns and proper nouns.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xiku.html#highlulani">Xiku</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">kimilli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mihu.html#highlulani">mihu</a>.

[3]Intransitives
If the only argument of the relative verb is the modified noun, the auxiliary is appended to the verb, and the relativiser is dropped. This auxiliary is given a mid-tone.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kiluqu.html#highlulani">kiluqu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">pi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">kimilli</a> the walking king
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/dissu'ahati.html#highlulani">dissu&rsquo;ahati</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulisa.html#highlulani">mulisa</a> the happy fool
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/bibu.html#highlulani">bibu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/na.html#highlulani">na</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/suma.html#highlulani">suma</a> the occasionally complaining me

Similar are intransitives utilising the case markers and other adpositions.

[3]Transitives
If the only arguments of the relative verb are the modified noun and a direct object, the verb is appended to the object, with or without the auxiliary, and the relativiser is dropped.

[2]Questions and Requests
Questions and requests are main clauses, but have the same auxiliary movement as dependent clauses, and thus are treated alongside them here.
[3]Interrogatives
An interrogative is a question sentence. There are two main types, polar questions and content questions.
Polar questions are one in which the answer is &ldquo;yes&rdquo; or &ldquo;no&rdquo;. They are spoken with a rising tone on the last word. The auxiliaries are used to answer.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">Lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/suma.html#highlulani">suma</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u</a>?
[e]<em>queen love</em> <small-caps>1tra prs;sta</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;Does the queen love me?&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">Ra&rsquo;u</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ji.html#highlulani">Ji</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ruku.html#highlulani">Ruku</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi.html#highlulani">Pi</a>.
[e]<small-caps>prs;sta  prs;neg  fut;gno  pst;sta</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;Yes.&rdquo; / &ldquo;No.&rdquo; / &ldquo;She will.&rdquo; / &ldquo;She did.&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">Lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nimalu.html#highlulani">nimalu</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ji.html#highlulani">ji</a>?
[e]<em>queen bear</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;neg</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present negative</span></span>
[e]&ldquo;Is the queen not a bear?&rdquo;
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ji.html#highlulani">Ji</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u.html#highlulani">Ra&rsquo;u</a>. / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/na.html#highlulani">Na</a>.
[e]<small-caps>prs;neg  prs;sta  prs;itr</small-caps>
[e]&ldquo;Yes, she&rsquo;s not.&rdquo; / &ldquo;No, she is.&rdquo; / &ldquo;Sometimes.&rdquo;
If the focus of the question is on a particular noun, that noun receives a falling tone.
Content questions are ones in which the expected answer is more than just &ldquo;yes&rdquo; or &ldquo;no&rdquo;. These questions have a rising tone on the main question word itself.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">Lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sama.html#highlulani">sama</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'u%3F.html#highlulani">ra&rsquo;u?</a>
[e]<em>queen love what</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;sta</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present stative</span></span>
[e]&ldquo;Whom does the queen love?&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">Kimilli</a> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/fu.html#highlulani">Fu</a> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cu'i.html#highlulani">Cu&rsquo;i</a>
[e]<em>king</em> / <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2tra</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person transitive</span></span> / <em>nothing</em>
[e]&ldquo;The king.&rdquo; / &ldquo;You.&rdquo; / &ldquo;No one.&rdquo;
[4]Quantities
Lulani questions regarding quantity or measurement are phrased thus:
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/filli.html#highlulani">Filli</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kika.html#highlulani">kika</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sama.html#highlulani">sama</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/huba.html#highlulani">huba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/rusa.html#highlulani">rusa</a>?
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>2int</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">second person intransitive</span></span> <em>interval-what breathe</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>pst;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">past gnomic</span></span><em>?</em>
[e]&ldquo;How old are you?&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kika.html#highlulani">Kika</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sama.html#highlulani">sama</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ku.html#highlulani">ku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'irri'a.html#highlulani">&#x294;irri&rsquo;a</a> (<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kiluqu.html#highlulani">kiluqu</a>) <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a>?
[e]<em>over-what</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>dat</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">dative</span></span><em>-Ir&igrave;a (walk)</em> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>prs;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">present gnomic</span></span><em>?</em>
[e]&ldquo;How far is it (to walk) to Ir&igrave;a?&rdquo;
[3]Imperatives
An imperative statement is an order.
Second person imperatives are directed to the listener. In these, the subject is dropped, a future auxiliary in the appropriate aspect is suffixed to the verb, and this verb complex is moved to the end of the sentence. These are spoken with a falling tone on the auxiliary.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">Lulani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lu'i.html#highlulani">lu&rsquo;i</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ruku.html#highlulani">ruku</a>!
[e]<em>queen love-</em><span class="tooltip"><small-caps>fut;gno</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">future gnomic</span></span>
[e]&ldquo;Love the queen!&rdquo;

[1]Noun Phrases
The full noun phrase is made up of these components in the following order:
[n]adposition-
case marker-
number
superlative
relative clause
main noun
-adjective
-conjunction
-genitive marker
[/n]
Hyphens in this list are used to mark where a space is not used to separate components.
Relative clauses include intransitives.
The only compulsory component of a noun phrase is the noun itself.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/faluki.html#highlulani">faluki</a> (vii) <em>journey</em>

&date=20170725
--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Comparatives
[2]Comparatives
The comparative marker is an adposition <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/su.html#highlulani">su</a> <em>than</em> placed on the noun being compared against. For &ldquo;little more&rdquo;, the qualifier <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tuci.html#highlulani">tuci</a> <em>half-do</em> is affixed to the verb, for &ldquo;a lot more&rdquo;, the qualifier is <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/rali.html#highlulani">rali</a> <em>intensely</em>.
[2]Equalatives
The equalative marker is <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ka.html#highlulani">ka</a> <em>as</em>, an adposition.
[2]Superlative
The superlative marker, contrary to the other two, is a particle <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/piba.html#highlulani">piba</a> placed before the verb.
&date=20170725

[1]Apocrypha
This section details particular categories of vocabulary items.
&date=20170716
--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Numbers
[2]Cardinal Numbers
High Lulani numbers are written with the positive digits (1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6 and 7), their negative counterparts (<overline>1</overline>, <overline>2</overline>, <overline>3</overline>, <overline>4</overline>, <overline>5</overline>, <overline>6</overline> and <overline>7</overline>) and a zero (0).
When writing out a number, each digit is worth fifteen times as much as the following digit. A period (fractional point: . ) is used to separate the integer part of the number from the mantissa. A comma (,) is used in the integer part to separate the digits into groupings of four, beginning from the fractional point.
[f]2 <em>two</em>
[e]5.<overline>3</overline> <em>four and four-fifths = five + (minus three &times; (fifteen ^ minus one</em></em>
[e]1<overline>7</overline> <em>eight = (one &times; fifteen) + (minus seven)</em>
[e]20 <em>thirty = (two &times; fifteen)</em>
[e]3<overline>2</overline>6 <em>six hundred and forty-one =
(three &times; (fifteen ^ two</em> + (minus two &times; fifteen) + six</em>
[e]<overline>1</overline>,34<overline>5</overline>3 <em>minus thirty-nine thousand, six hundred and seventy-two =
(minus one &times; (fifteen ^ four</em> + (three &times; (fifteen ^ three</em> +
(four &times; (fifteen ^ two</em> + (minus five &times; fifteen) + three</em>
[3]One-digit Numbers
Here are the names for the one-digit numbers:
