[3]Two-digit Numbers
Numbers between 1<overline>7</overline> and 16 are composed of the prefix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sa.html#highlulani">sa</a> and the final two syllables of the number, except for <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/salura.html#highlulani">salura</a> (not <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sara.html#highlulani">sara</a>) 12.
Round numbers, <em>i.e.:</em> numbers ending with a single zero, use the suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/-hha.html#highlulani">-hha</a>.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sahha.html#highlulani">sahha</a> 10
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/rahha.html#highlulani">rahha</a> 20
[e]<strong>kifihha</strong> 30
All other two digit numbers, except for 22, are formed by juxtaposing the tens digit with the units.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mullu.html#highlulani">mullu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kifi.html#highlulani">kifi</a> <overline>1</overline>3
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xita.html#highlulani">xita</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/salumi.html#highlulani">salumi</a> 17
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nuru.html#highlulani">nuru</a> 24
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kifi.html#highlulani">kifi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/laffi.html#highlulani">laffi</a> 3<overline>5</overline>
The word for 22, the exception, is <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ranira.html#highlulani">ranira</a>.
[3]Three- and Four-digit Numbers
Three- and four-digit numbers are divided into the number of hundreds, and the remainder. This remainder is always the last two digits of the number.
The word for 100 is <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a>.
Other three-digit numbers beginning with a 1 are formed by prefixing <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> to the remainder.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nuru.html#highlulani">nuru</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kannu.html#highlulani">kannu</a> 14<overline>2</overline>
Three- and four-digit numbers greater than this are formed by appending <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> to the number of hundreds, which is then followed by the remainder as a separate word.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/guhi.html#highlulani">guhi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/bila.html#highlulani">bila</a> 56<overline>3</overline>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sahha.html#highlulani">sahha</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kifi.html#highlulani">kifi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nuru.html#highlulani">nuru</a> 1034
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kannu.html#highlulani">kannu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/missu.html#highlulani">missu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mullu.html#highlulani">mullu</a> <overline>2</overline>2<overline>4</overline><overline>1</overline>
In any of these cases, if the remainder is zero, it is left off.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mullu.html#highlulani">mullu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> <overline>1</overline>00
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> 200
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sa.html#highlulani">sa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/guhi.html#highlulani">guhi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> 1500
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/bila.html#highlulani">bila</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/salumi.html#highlulani">salumi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> <overline>3</overline>700
[3]Higher and Lower Order Numbers
When a number is written out in digits, each set of four digits from the fractional point makes up a group. The group furthest from the fractional point may not have this full quota of digits. An index marker notes the identity of a particular group.
The index marker is composed of the prefix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a> followed by the number of groups between this one and the fractional point. Positive index numbers are for the integer part of the number, and negative index numbers are for the mantissa.
The index marker is suffixed to the group word.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xita.html#highlulani">xita</a> 1,0000
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a> 1,0000,0000
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kifi.html#highlulani">kifi</a> 1,0000,0000,0000
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mullu.html#highlulani">mullu</a> 0.0001
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sa.html#highlulani">sa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/missu.html#highlulani">missu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xita.html#highlulani">xita</a> 1<overline>4</overline>,0000
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ranira.html#highlulani">ranira</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xita.html#highlulani">xita</a> 122,0000
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/'usi.html#highlulani">&rsquo;usi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/takki.html#highlulani">takki</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mullu.html#highlulani">mullu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xita.html#highlulani">xita</a> 6<overline>1</overline>2,0000
There is nothing preventing an index-marked number being used within another index marker, although the second <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a> is usually geminated.
[f]<strong>pappaxita</strong> 1,0000<sup>1,0000</sup>
[e]<strong>papappaxita</strong> 1,0000<sup>1,0000^1,0000</sup>
[3]Non-integral Numbers
[4]Reading Mantissas
There are two ways to read a mantissa.
One uses the above method of index markers, and the second reads out the digits in pairs or individually. These methods are often combined: using index markers for the first digit groups, and then continuing to read digits separately.
[4]Repeating and Reflecting Strings
All rational numbers end with a repeating string of digits. For some numbers, this string is &ldquo;0&rdquo;. In non-zero cases, the word <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tuni.html#highlulani">tuni</a> repeat is inserted before the repeating string. The string must be read out with individual digits.
There are also numbers for which the repeating string can be cut in half, with digits in the second half being the negative of the digits in the first half. For these, only the first half is read out, with the word <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mala.html#highlulani">mala</a> reflect inserted.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tuni.html#highlulani">tuni</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/guhi.html#highlulani">guhi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a> 0.5252&hellip;
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qihha.html#highlulani">qihha</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xita.html#highlulani">xita</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tuni.html#highlulani">tuni</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/guhi.html#highlulani">guhi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a> 0.15252&hellip;
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pa.html#highlulani">pa</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qihha.html#highlulani">qihha</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xita.html#highlulani">xita</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mala.html#highlulani">mala</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/guhi.html#highlulani">guhi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a> 0.152<overline>5</overline><overline>2</overline>52<overline>5</overline><overline>2</overline>&hellip;
[4]Fractions
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ki.html#highlulani">ki</a> separates the numerator from the denominator. <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/saki.html#highlulani">Saki</a> is used if the numerator is 1. There is also a commonly used variant for &frac12;: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'ima.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ima</a>.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'ima.html#highlulani">&rsquo;ima</a> / <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/saki.html#highlulani">saki</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a> &frac12;
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/saki.html#highlulani">saki</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kifi.html#highlulani">kifi</a> &frac13;
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kifi.html#highlulani">kifi</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ki.html#highlulani">ki</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/n/nuru.html#highlulani">nuru</a> &frac34;
[2]Ordinal Numbers
Ordinal numbers are used to mark position in a line or a list.
The first two ordinal numbers are suppletive, that is, they are not related to their cardinals. All other ordinals are formed by adding the suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/u/-uju.html#highlulani">-uju</a> <small-caps>ord</small-caps> to the cardinal number.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/bijju.html#highlulani">bijju</a> <em>first</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/matta.html#highlulani">matta</a> <em>second</em>
[e]<strong>kifuju</strong> <em>third</em>
[e]<strong>nuruju</strong> <em>fourth</em>
[e]<strong>salumuju</strong> <em>seventh</em>
[e]<strong>saqikkuju</strong> <em>fifteenth</em>
[e]<strong>saxituju</strong> <em>sixteenth</em>
[e]<strong>takkuju</strong> <em>two hundred and twenty-fifth</em>
[2]Using Numbers
Ordinal and cardinal numbers are used in noun phrases, and are inserted between any case markers or adpositions, and the noun.
[f]<strong>nuruju</strong> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kimilli.html#highlulani">kimilli</a>
[e]<em>four-</em><small-caps>ord</small-caps> <em>king</em>
[e]&ldquo;the fourth king.&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kalu.html#highlulani">kalu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/salumi.html#highlulani">salumi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/lulani.html#highlulani">lulani</a>
[e]<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>abl</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">ablative</span></span><em>-seven queen</em>
[e]&ldquo;due to the seven queens.&rdquo;
Numbers can be suffixed to a noun to denote not the quantity, but a quality.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/salumi.html#highlulani">salumi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sinnadi.html#highlulani">sinnadi</a>
[e]seven story-<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>nmn</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">nominaliser</span></span>
[e]&ldquo;seven books&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sinna.html#highlulani">sinna</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/salumi.html#highlulani">salumi</a>
[e]<em>story</em>-<em>seven</em>
[e]&ldquo;septet&rdquo;
The number <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a> <em>two</em> can be used in this way to refer to a pair of something that is usually found in pairs
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/l/luffu.html#highlulani">luffu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a> <em>eyes</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/i/'itikku.html#highlulani">&rsquo;itikku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a> <em>breasts</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tiba.html#highlulani">tiba</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra.html#highlulani">ra</a> <em>legs</em>
&date=20180317--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Colours
The basis colour terms are all verbs:
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/baju.html#highlulani">baju</a> <em>blue</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sa.html#highlulani">sa</a> <em>yellow</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a> <em>red</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/millu.html#highlulani">millu</a> <em>brown</em>
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ki''a.html#highlulani">ki&#x294;a</a> <em>white</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/ga.html#highlulani">ga</a> <em>black</em>
<img src="http://www.tinellb.com/images/colourwheel.png">
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/baju.html#highlulani">Baju</a> <em>blue</em> covers both light and dark blue, the darkest violets, and all but the lightest shades of green. <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sa.html#highlulani">Sa</a> <em>yellow</em> covers the lightest shades of orange and green, as well as standard yellow. <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">Miku</a> <em>red</em> refers to all of red and pink, light purples and most of the orange spectrum, however, dark orange is subsumed under <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/millu.html#highlulani">millu</a> <em>brown</em>.
The figure above shows which shades are referred to by which term. <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ki''a.html#highlulani">Ki&#x294;a</a> <em>white</em> is used to refer to very light greys, as well as the usual white. <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/ga.html#highlulani">Ga</a> <em>black</em> is used to refer to the darker greys, tending towards the black.
In continuous aspects, these denote the colour of an object. With discrete aspects, these refer to a change in colour.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pu'iba.html#highlulani">Pu&rsquo;iba</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a>.
[e]<em>ball</em> <small-caps>prs;gno</small-caps> <em>red</em>.
[e]&ldquo;The ball is red.&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'ara.html#highlulani">&#x294;ara</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/d/disi.html#highlulani">disi</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/c/cani.html#highlulani">cani</a> <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a>.
[e]<em>face</em>-<small-caps>3ani;gen prs;dyn</small-caps> <em>red</em>.
[e]&ldquo;She blushed.&rdquo;
Each of these terms can be compounded to refer to specific hues.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/miku.html#highlulani">miku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/mulu.html#highlulani">mulu</a> <em>blood red</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/baju.html#highlulani">baju</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kunubi.html#highlulani">kunubi</a> <em>sky blue</em>
[e]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/ki''a.html#highlulani">ki&#x294;a</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/m/masi.html#highlulani">masi</a> <em>snow white</em>
&date=20170725
--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Kinship
[2]Marriage
<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ju'iduku.html#highlulani">Ju&rsquo;iduku</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ru.html#highlulani">ru</a> <em>marriage</em> is the life-bonding of two people. It is intended to be eternal, but can be broken if requested by either partner. It is not an exclusive arrangement, and one can be involved in concurrent marriages.
A bonded person is called a <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/silu.html#highlulani">silu</a> <em>spouse</em> when using possessive pronouns, and  <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/x/xalli.html#highlulani">xalli</a> <em>married person</em> otherwise.
[2]Nuclear Family
The words <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kitisu.html#highlulani">kitisu</a> <em>father</em> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/julliga.html#highlulani">julliga</a> <em>mother</em> usually refer to biological parents, but can be applied to the main guardians if the biological parents are not around. These are used without possessives, except for the inalienable genitive marker <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/q/qa.html#highlulani">qa</a> <high-lulani>q</high-lulani> <span class="tooltip"><small-caps>gen</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">genitive</span></span>
The following table shows the possessive forms:
[t]|h mother |h father
h 1st person | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi'apagu.html#highlulani">pi&rsquo;apagu</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sappagu.html#highlulani">sappagu</a>
h 2nd person | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pihaba.html#highlulani">pihaba</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sabba.html#highlulani">sabba</a>
h 3rd person topic | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pihasu'a.html#highlulani">pihasu&rsquo;a</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sassu'a.html#highlulani">sassu&rsquo;a</a>
h 3rd person animate | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi'adisi.html#highlulani">pi&rsquo;adisi</a> | <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/saddisi.html#highlulani">saddisi</a>[/t]

mother:
[e]first person: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pi'apagu.html#highlulani">pi&rsquo;apagu</a>
[e]second person: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/p/pihaba.html#highlulani">pihaba</a>

[e]third person animate: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/saddisi.html#highlulani">saddisi</a>
[/d]
There are two terms for children: <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tu.html#highlulani">tu</a> <em>offspring</em> for postnatal children, <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/a/'appu.html#highlulani">&rsquo;appu</a> <em>foetus</em> for antenatal. Both of these are gender-neutral, and are most often used with possessives.
There can be a suffixed <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ju'i.html#highlulani">ju&rsquo;i</a> <em>link</em> for spouses&rsquo; offspring and parents&rsquo; spouses.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/s/sappagu.html#highlulani">sappagu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ju'i.html#highlulani">ju&rsquo;i</a>
[e]father;1<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>gen</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">genitive</span></span>-link
[e]&ldquo;my step-father&rdquo;
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/t/tu.html#highlulani">tu</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/j/ju'i.html#highlulani">ju&rsquo;i</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/b/ba.html#highlulani">ba</a>
[e]offspring-link-2<span class="tooltip"><small-caps>gen</small-caps><span class="tooltip-text">genitive</span></span>
[e]&ldquo;your step-daughter&rdquo;
Other kinship terms began as nuclear family names, but were thence extended across a generation. So <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kaqqa.html#highlulani">kaqqa</a> <em>elder sibling</em> and <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/k/kica.html#highlulani">kica</a> <em>younger sibling</em> can also be applied to cousins.
&date=20180329--------------------------------------------------3
[1]Honorifics
The suffix <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/f/-fi.html#highlulani">-fi</a> can be added to abstract and inanimate nouns to show deference.
Honorifics for people consist of a word prefixed to the person&rsquo;s name. The general honorific is <a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/g/gusu.html#highlulani">gusu</a> (person).
The honorific can be a job title.
[f]<a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/h/hisuba.html#highlulani">hisuba</a><a href="http://dictionary.tinellb.com/r/ra'ani.html#highlulani">Ra&rsquo;ani</a> (Administrator Ryan)
